ad 54 -lrb- au 807 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 1 -- -rrb- at the death of claudius the leadership on most just principle belong to britannicus who have be bear a legitimate son of claudius and in physical development be beyond what would have be expect of he year yet by law the power pass to nero on account of he adoption no claim indeed be stronger than that of arm every one who possess superior force have always the appearance of both say and do what be more just so nero have first dispose of claudius 's will and have succeed he as master of the whole empire put britannicus and he sister out of the way why then should one stop to lament the misfortune of other victim -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- the follow sign of dominion have be observe in he career at he birth just before dawn ray not cast by any beam of sunlight yet visible surround he form and a certain astrologer from this and from the motion of the star at that time and they relation to one another divine two thing in regard to he -- that he would rule and that he would murder he mother agrippina on hearing this become for the moment so beside herself as actually to cry out : let he kill I if only he shall rule later she be destine to repent bitterly of she prayer some people become so steep in folly that if they expect to obtain some blessing mingle with evil they at once through they anxiety for the advantage pay no heed to the detriment when the time for the latter also come they be cast down and would choose not to have secure even the greatest good thing yet domitius the father of nero have a sufficient previous intimation of he son 's come baseness and licentiousness not by any oracle but through the nature of he own and agrippina 's character and he declare : it be impossible for any good man to be bear from I and from she as time go on the finding of a serpent skin around nero 's neck when he be but a boy cause the seer to say : he shall acquire great power from the aged man serpent be think to slough off they old age with they old skin and so get power -lrb- sidenote : -- 3 -- -rrb- nero be seventeen year of age when he begin to rule he first enter the camp and after read to the soldier all that seneca have write he promise they as much as claudius have be accustom to give before the senate he read such a considerable document -- this too write by seneca -- that it be vote the statement should be inscribe on a silver tablet and should be read every time the new consul take up the duty of they office consequently those who hear he make themselves ready to enjoy a good reign accord to the letter of the compilation at first agrippina -lrb- in company with palla a vulgar and tiresome man -rrb- manage all affair pertain to the empire and she and she son go about together often recline in the same litter usually however she would be carry and he would follow alongside it be she who transact business with embassy and send letter to people and governor and king when this have go on for a considerable time it arouse the displeasure of seneca and burrus who be both the most sensible and the most influential of the adviser of nero the one be he teacher and the other be prefect of the pretorian they take the follow occasion to stop this method of procedure a embassy of armenian have arrive and agrippina wish to ascend the platform from which nero be talk with they the two man see she approach persuade the young man to go down before she could reach there and meet he mother pretend some form of greet after that be do they do not return again make some excuse to prevent the foreigner from see the flaw in the empire subsequently they labor to keep any public business from be again commit to she hand -lrb- sidenote : -- 4 -- -rrb- when they have accomplish this they themselves take charge of the entire empire and give it the very best and fairest management that they could nero be not in general fond of affair and be glad to live at leisure -lrb- the reason indeed that he have previously distrust he mother and now be fond of she lay in the fact that now he be free to enjoy himself and the government be be carry on no less well and he adviser after consultation make many change in exist custom abolish some thing altogether and pass a number of new law -rrb- they let nero sow he wild oats with the intention of bring about in he through the satisfaction of all he desire a changed attitude of mind while in the meantime no great damage should be do to public interest surely they must have know that a young and self-willed spirit when rear in unreproved license and in absolute authority so far from become satiated by the indulgence of its passion be ruin more and more by these very agency indeed nero at first give but simple dinner he revel he drunkenness he amours be moderate afterward as no one reprove he for they and public business be carry forward none the worse for all of it he begin to believe that what he do be right and that he could carry he practice to even greater length -lrb- consequently he begin to indulge in each of these pursuit in a more open and precipitate fashion and in case he guardian give he any warning or he mother any rebuke he would appear abashed while they be present and promise to reform but as soon as they be go he would again become the slave of he desire and yield to those who be drag he in the other direction -- a straight course down hill -rrb- next he come to despise instruction inasmuch as he be always hear from he associate do _ you _ submit to this or do _ you _ fear these people do not you know that you be caesar have not you the authority over they rather than they over you he be also animated by obstinacy not wish to acknowledge he mother as superior and himself as inferior nor to admit the greater good sense of seneca and burrus -lrb- sidenote : -- 5 -- -rrb- finally he pass the possibility of be shame dash to the ground and trample under foot all they suggestion and begin to follow in the step of gaius when he have once feel a desire to emulate he he quite outdo he for he believe that the imperial power must manifest itself among other way by allow no one to surpass it even in the vilest deed -lrb- as he be praise for this by the crowd and receive many pleasant compliment from they he give himself no rest he doings be at first confine to he home and associate but be later on carry abroad thus he attach a mighty disgrace to the whole roman race and commit many outrage upon the individual compose it innumerable act of violence and insult of rape and murder be commit both by the emperor himself and by those who at one time or another have influence with he and as certainly and inevitably follow in all such practice -rrb- great sum of money naturally be spend great sum unjustly procure and great sum seize by force for under no circumstance be nero niggardly here be a illustration he have order no less than two hundred and fifty myriad at one time to be give to doryphorus who attend to the state document of he empire agrippina have it all pile in a heap hope by show he the money all together to make he change he mind instead he ask how much the mass before he amount to and when he be inform he double it say : i be not aware that i have allow he so little it can clearly be see then that as a result of the magnitude of he expenditure he would quickly exhaust the treasure in the royal vault and quickly need new revenue hence unusual tax be impose and the property of the well-to-do be not leave intact some lose they possession to spite he and other destroy themselves with they livelihood similarly he hate and make away with some other who have no considerable wealth for if they possess any excellent trait or be of a good family he become suspicious that they dislike he -lrb- sidenote : -- 6 -- -rrb- such be the general characteristic of nero i shall now proceed to detail in the matter of horse-race nero grow so enthusiastic that he adorn famous race-horse that have pass they prime with the regular street costume for man and honor they with money for they fodder the horsebreeder and charioteer elate at this enthusiasm of he proceed to abuse unjustifiably even the praetor and consul but aulus fabricius when praetor finding that they refuse to hold contest on fair term dispense with they entirely he train dog to draw chariot and introduce they in place of horse when this be do the wearer of the white and of the red immediately enter they chariot : but as the green and the blues would not even then participate nero at he own cost give the prize to the horse and the regular program of the circus be carry out agrippina show readiness to attack the greatest undertaking as be evidence by she cause the death of marcus julius silanus to whom she send some of the poison with which she have treacherously murder she husband silanus be governor of asia and be in no respect inferior to the general character of he family it be for this more than for anything else she say that she kill he not wish to have he prefer before nero by reason of the latter 's manner of life moreover she turn everything into trade and gather money from the most insignificant and basest source laelianus who be despatch to armenia in place of pollio have be assign to the command of the night watch and he be no better than pollio for while surpass he in reputation he be all the more insatiable in respect to gain -lrb- sidenote : ad 55 -lrb- au 808 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 7 -- -rrb- agrippina find a grievance in the fact that she be no longer supreme in affair of the palace it be chiefly because of acte acte have be bring as a slave from asia she catch the fancy of nero be adopt into the family of attalus and be cherish much more carefully than be nero 's wife octavium agrippina indignant at this and at other matter first attempt to rebuke he and set herself to humiliating he associate some by beating and by get rid of other but when she accomplish nothing she take it greatly to heart and remark to he : it be i who make you emperor just as if she have the power to take away the authority from he again she do not comprehend that every form of independent power give to any one by a private citizen immediately cease to be the property of the giver and belong to the one who receive it to use against he benefactor britannicus nero murder treacherously by poison and then as the skin be turn livid by the action of the drug he smear the body with gypsum but as it be be carry through the forum a heavy rain fall while the gypsum be still damp wash it all away so that the horror be expose not only to comment but to view -lrb- after britannicus be dead seneca and burrus cease to give careful attention to public interest and be satisfy if they might manage they conservatively and still preserve they life consequently nero now make himself conspicuous by give free rein to all he desire without fear of retribution he behavior begin to be absolutely insensate as be show for instance by he punish a certain knight antonius as a seller of poison and by further burn the poison publicly he take great credit for this action as well as for prosecute some person who have tamper with will but other people only laugh to see he punish he own act in the person of other -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 8 -- -rrb- he secret act of licentiousness be many both at home and throughout the city by night and by day he use to frequent the tavern and wander about everywhere like a private person any number of beating and insult take place in this connection and the evil spread to the theater so that those who work as dancer and who have charge of the horse pay no attention either to praetor or to consul they be disorderly themselves and lead other to be the same while nero not only do not restrain they even by word but stir they up all the more he delight in they action and use to be secretly convey in a litter into the theater where unseen by the rest he watch the proceedings indeed he forbid the soldier who have usually be in attendance at all public gathering to appear there any longer the reason he assign be that they ought not to superintend anything but strictly military affair but he true purpose be to afford those who wish to raise a disturbance the amplest scope he make use of the same excuse in reference to he not allow any soldier to attend he mother say that no one except the emperor ought to be guard by they in this way he display he enmity toward the mass and as for he mother he be already openly at variance with she everything that they say to each other or that the imperial pair do each day be report outside the palace yet it do not all reach the public and hence conjecture be make to supply miss detail and different version arise what be conceivable as happen in view of the baseness and lewdness of the pair be noised abroad as have already take place and report possess some credibility be believe as true the populace see agrippina now for the first time without pretorian take care not to fall in with she even by accident and if any one do chance to meet she he would hastily get out of the way without say a word -lrb- sidenote : -- 9 -- -rrb- at one spectacle man on horseback overcome bull while ride along beside they and the knight who serve as nero 's personal guard bring down with they javelin four hundred bear and three hundred lion on the same occasion thirty knight belong to the military fight in the arena the emperor sanction such proceedings openly secretly however he carry on nocturnal revel throughout the length and breadth of the city insulting the woman practice lewdness on boy strip those whom he encounter striking wound murder he have a idea that he incognito be impenetrable for he use all sort of different costume and false hair at different time : but he would be recognize by he retinue and by he deed no one else would have dare to commit so many and such gross outrage so recklessly -lrb- sidenote : ad 56 -lrb- au 809 -rrb- -rrb- it be become unsafe even for a person to stay at home be striking nero the suicide of montanus follow hard after -lrb- sidenote : ad 57 -lrb- au 810 -rrb- -rrb- in the course of produce a spectacle at one of the theater he suddenly fill the place with that she might feel a desire to use the vessel continually -lrb- sidenote : -- 13 -- -rrb- when they reach baulus he give for several day most costly dinner at which he show great solicitude in shape the situation to this extent -lrb- footnote : adopt reiske 's conjecture _ nv _ -rrb- then rise from dinner about midnight he embrace she and strain she to he breast kiss she eye and hand prepare but the sea would not endure the tragedy about to be enact on it nor would it submit to assume responsibility for the deception work by the monstrous contrivance : therefore though the ship for this bear nero -lrb- sidenote : -- 14 -- -rrb- thus be agrippina daughter of germanicus grandchild of agrippa descendant of augustus slay by the very son to whom she have give the sovereignty and -rrb- proclaim he by name there stand caesar on the stage wear the garb of a singing zither-player speak the emperor : my lord of you kindness give I ear then do the augustus sing to the zither a hand and toga at every utterance and draw other on to do the same indeed nero have ready a peculiar corps of about five thousand soldier call augustan these would begin the applause and all the rest however loath be oblige to shout aloud with they -- except thrasea he would never stoop to such conduct but the rest and especially the prominent man gather with alacrity even when in grief and join performance he entertain the people at a feast on boat on the site of the naval battle give by augustus : thence at midnight he sail through a canal into the tiber -lrb- sidenote : ad 60 -lrb- au 813 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 21 -- -rrb- this then he do to celebrate the shaving of he chin in behalf of he preservation and the continuance of he authority -- thus he give notice -- he institute than often belong to woman it be she who gather the army to the number of nearly twelve myriad and ascend a tribunal of marshy soil make after the roman fashion in person she be very tall with a most sturdy figure and a pierce glance she voice be harsh a great mass of yellow hair fall below she waist and a large golden necklace clasp she throat wound about she be a tunic of every conceivable color and over it a thick chlamy have be fasten with a brooch this be she constant attire she now grasp a spear to aid she in terrifying all beholder and speak as follow : -- -lrb- sidenote : -- 3 -- -rrb- you have have actual experience of the difference between freedom and slavery hence though some of you previously through ignorance of which be better may have be deceive by the alluring announcement of the roman yet now that you have try both you have learn how great a mistake you make by prefer a self-imposed despotism to you ancestral mode of life you have come to recognize how far superior be the poverty of independence to wealth in servitude what treatment have we meet with that be not most outrageous that be not most grievous ever since these man insinuate themselves into britain have we not be deprive of we most numerous and we greatest possession entire while for what remain we must pay tax besides pasturing and till all the various region for they do we not contribute a yearly sum for we very body how much better it would have be to be sell to master once and for all than to ransom ourselves annually and possess empty name of freedom how much better to have be slay and perish rather than go about with subservient head yet what have i say even die be not free from expense among they and you know what fee we deposit on behalf of the dead throughout the rest of mankind death free even those who be in slavery only in the case of the roman do the very dead live for they profit why be it that though none of we have any money -- and how or whence should we get it -- we be strip and despoil like a murderer 's victim how should the roman grow milder in process of time when they have conduct themselves so toward we at the very start -- a period when all man show consideration for even newly capture beast -lrb- sidenote : -- 4 -- -rrb- but to tell the truth it be we who have make ourselves responsible for all these evil in allow they so much as to set foot on the island in the first place instead of expel they at once as we do they famous julius caesar -- yes in not make the idea of attempt the voyage formidable to they while they be as yet far off as it be to augustus and to gaius caligulum so great a island or rather in one sense a continent encircle by water do we inhabit a veritable world of we own and so far be we separate by the ocean from all the rest of mankind that we have be believe to dwell on a different earth and under a different sky and some of they wisest man be not previously sure of even we exact name yet for all this we have be scorn and trample under foot by man who know naught else than how to secure gain still let we even at this late day if not before fellow-citizen friend and relative -- for i deem you all relative in that you inhabit a single island and be call by -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- greek : chechlaemenous -rrb- -lrb- van herwerden -rrb- -rrb- one common name -- let we do we duty while the memory of freedom still abide within we that we may leave both the name and the fact of it to we child for if we utterly lose sight of the happy condition amid which we be bear and breed what pray will they do rear in bondage -lrb- sidenote : -- 5 -- -rrb- this i say not to inspire you with a hatred of present circumstance -- that hatred be already apparent -- nor with a fear of the future -- that fear you already have -- but to commend you because of you own accord you choose to do just what you ought and to thank you for cooperate so readily with I and you own self at once be nowise afraid of the roman they be not more numerous than be we nor yet braver and the proof be that they have protect themselves with helmet and breastplate and greave and furthermore have equip they camp with palisade and wall and ditch to make sure that they shall suffer no harm by any hostile assault -lrb- footnote : corruption in the text emend by reiske -rrb- they fear impel they to choose this method rather than engage in any active work like we we enjoy such a superabundance of bravery that we regard tent as safer than wall and we shield as afford greater protection than they whole suit of mail as a consequence we when victorious can capture they and when overcome by force can elude they and should we ever choose to retreat we can conceal ourselves in swamp and mountain so inaccessible that we can be neither find nor take the enemy however can neither pursue any one by reason of they heavy armor nor yet flee and if they ever should slip away from we take refuge in certain designate spot there too they be sure to be enclose as in a trap these be some of the respects in which they be vastly inferior to we and other be they inability to bear up under hunger thirst cold or heat as we can for they require shade and protection they require knead bread and wine and oil and if the supply of any of these thing fail they they simply perish for we on the other hand any root or grass serve as bread any plant juice as olive oil any water as wine any tree as a house indeed this very region be to we a acquaintance and ally but to they unknown and hostile as for the river we swim they naked but they even with boat can not cross easily let we therefore go against they trust boldly to good fortune let we show they that they be hare and fox try to rule dog and wolf -lrb- sidenote : -- 6 -- -rrb- at these word employ a species of divination she let a hare escape from she bosom and as it run in what they consider a lucky direction the whole multitude shout with pleasure and buduica raise she hand to heaven speak : i thank thee andraste -lrb- footnote : not much information be preserved regard this indigenous goddess of britain reimar assert that she be practically identical with boccharte astarte or venus -rrb- and call upon thee who be a woman be myself also a woman that rule not burden-bearing egyptian like nitocri nor merchant assyrian like semiramis -lrb- of these thing we have hear from the roman -rrb- nor even the roman themselves as do messalina first and later agrippina -- at present they chief be nero in name a man in fact a woman as be show by he singing he play the cithara he adorning himself : -- but rule as i do man of britain that know not how to till the soil or ply a trade yet be thoroughly verse in the art of war and hold all thing common even child and wife wherefore the latter possess the same valor as the male : be therefore queen of such man and such woman i supplicate and pray thee for victory and salvation and liberty against man insolent unjust insatiable impious -- if indeed we ought to term those creature man who wash in warm water eat artificial dainty drink unmixed wine anoint themselves with myrrh sleep on soft couch with boy for bedfellow -lrb- and past they prime at that -rrb- be slave to a zither-player yes a inferior zither-player wherefore may this domitia-nero _ woman _ reign no more over you or over I : let the wench sing and play the despot over the roman they surely deserve to be in slavery to such a be whose tyranny they have patiently bear already this long time but may we mistress ever look to thee alone as we head -lrb- sidenote : -- 7 -- -rrb- after a harangue of this general nature buduica lead she army against the roman the latter chance to be without a leader for the reason that paulinus they commander have go on a expedition to mona a island near britain this enable she to sack and plunder two roman city and as i say she work indescribable slaughter person capture by the briton undergo every form of most frightful treatment the conqueror commit the most atrocious and bestial outrage for instance they hang up naked the noblest and most distinguished woman cut off they breast and sew they to they mouth to make the victim appear to be eat they after that they impale they on sharp skewer run perpendicularly the whole length of the body all this they do to the accompaniment of sacrifice banquet and exhibition of insolence in all of they sacred place but chiefly in the grove of andate -- that be the name of they personification of victory to whom they pay the most excessive reverence -lrb- sidenote : -- 8 -- -rrb- it happen that paulinus have already bring mona to term hence on learning of the disaster in britain he at once set sail thither from mona he be unwilling to risk a conflict with the barbarian immediately for he fear they number and they frenzy therefore he be for postpone the battle to a more convenient season but as he grow short of food and the barbarian do not desist from press he hard he be compel though contrary to he plan to enter into a engagement with they buduica herself head a army of about twenty-three myriad of man ride on a chariot and assign the rest to they several station now paulinus could not extend he phalanx the width of she whole line for even if the man have be draw up only one deep they would not have stretch far enough so inferior be they in number : nor do he dare to join battle with one compact force for fear he should be surround and cut down accordingly he separate he army into three division in order to fight at several point at once and he make each of the division so strong that it could not easily be break through while order and arrange he man he likewise exhort they say : -lrb- sidenote : -- 9 -- -rrb- up fellow-soldier up man of rome show these pest how much even in misfortune we surpass they it be a shame for you now to lose ingloriously what but a short while ago you gain by you valor often have we ourselves and also we father with far fewer number than we have at the present conquer far more numerous antagonist fear not the host of they or they rebellion : they boldness rest on nothing better than headlong rashness unaided by arm and exercise fear not because they have set on fire a few city : they take these not by force nor after a battle but one be betray and the other abandon do you now exact from they the proper penalty for these deed that so they may learn by actual experience what they undertake when they wrong such man as we -lrb- sidenote : -- 10 -- -rrb- after speak these word to some he come to a second group and say : now be the occasion now fellow-soldier for zeal for daring if to-day you prove yourselve brave man you will recover what have slip from you grasp if you overcome this enemy no one else will any longer withstand we by one such battle you will both make sure of you present possession and subdue whatever be leave all soldier station anywhere else will emulate you and foe will be terror-stricken therefore since it be in you own hand either to rule fearlessly all mankind both the nation that you father leave under you control and those which you yourselve have gain in addition or else to be bereft of they utterly choose rather to be free to rule to live in wealth to enjoy prosperity than through indolence to suffer the reverse of these condition -lrb- sidenote : -- 11 -- -rrb- after make a address of this sort to the group in question he come up to the third division and say also to they : you have hear what sort of act these wretch have commit against we nay more you have even see some of they therefore choose either yourselve to suffer the same treatment as previous victim and furthermore to be drive entirely out of britain or else through victory to avenge those that perish and also to give to the rest of mankind a example of mild clemency toward the obedient of necessary severity toward the rebellious i entertain the highest hope of victory for we side count on the following factor : first the assistance of the god they usually cooperate with the party that have be wrong : second we inherit bravery we be roman and have show ourselves superior to all mankind in various instance of valor : next we experience we have defeat and subdue these very man that be now array against we : last we good name it be not worthy opponent but we slave with whom we be come in conflict person who enjoy freedom and self-government only so far as we allow it yet even should the outcome prove contrary to we hope -- and i will not shrink from mention even this contingency -- it be better for we to fall fight bravely than to be capture and impale to see we own entrails cut out to be spit on red hot skewer to perish dissolve in boiling water when we have fall into the power of creature that be very beast savage lawless godless let we therefore either beat they or die on the spot britain shall be a noble memorial to we even though all subsequent roman should be drive from it for in any case we body shall forever possess the land -lrb- sidenote : -- 12 -- -rrb- at the conclusion of exhortation of this sort and other like they he raise the signal for battle thereupon they approach each other the barbarian make a great outcry intermingle with menacing incantation but the roman silently and in order until they come within a javelin 's throw of the enemy then while the foe be advance against they at a walk the roman start at a give word and charge they at full speed and when the clash come easily break through the oppose rank but as they be surround by the great number they have to be fight everywhere at once they struggle take many form in the first place light-armed troops might be in conflict with light-armed heavy-armed be array against heavy-armed cavalry join issue with cavalry and against the chariot of the barbarian the roman archer would be contend again the barbarian would assail the roman with a rush of they chariot knock they helter-skelter but since they fight without breastplate would be themselves repulse by the arrow horseman would upset foot-soldier and foot-soldier strike down horseman some form in close order would go to meet the chariot and other would be scatter by they some would come to close quarter with the archer and rout they whereas other be content to dodge they shaft at a distance : and all these thing go on not at one spot but in the three division at once they contend for a long time both party be animated by the same zeal and daring finally though late in the day the roman prevail have slay number in the battle beside the wagon or in the wood : they also capture many alive still not a few make they escape and go on to prepare to fight a second time meanwhile however buduica fall sick and die the briton mourn she deeply and give she a costly burial but as they themselves be this time really defeat they scatter to they home -- so far the history of affair in britain -lrb- sidenote : ad 62 -lrb- au 815 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 13 -- -rrb- in rome nero have before this send away octavium augusta on account of he concubine sabina and subsequently he put she to death this he do in spite of the opposition of burrus who try to prevent he send she away and once say to he : well then give she back she dowry -lrb- by which he mean the sovereignty -rrb- indeed burrus use such unmitigated frankness that on one occasion when he be ask by the emperor a second time for a opinion on matter regard which he have already make clear he attitude he answer bluntly : when i have once have my say about anything do not ask I again so nero disposed of he by poison he also appoint to command the pretorian a certain ofonius tigillinus who outstrip all he contemporary in licentiousness and bloodiness -lrb- it be he who win nero away from they and make light of he colleague rufus -rrb- -lrb- footnote : _ foenius rufus _ -rrb- to he the famous sentence of pythia be say to have be direct she have prove the only exception when all the other attendant of octavium have join sabina in attack they mistress despise the one because she be in misfortune and toady to the other because she influence be strong pythia alone have refuse though cruelly tortured to utter lie against octavium and finally as tigillinus continue to urge she she spit in he face say : my mistress 's privy part be cleaner tigillinus than you mouth -lrb- sidenote : -- 14 -- -rrb- the trouble of he relative nero turn into laughter and that he would have spare he have he be aware of this fact beforehand and though he spend practically he whole existence in tavern life he forbid other to sell in tavern anything boil save vegetable and pea-soup he put palla out of the way because the latter have accumulate great wealth that could be count by the ten thousand myriad likewise he be very liable to peevishness that show in he behavior and at such time he would not speak a word to he servant or freedman but write on tablet whatever he want as well as any order that he have to give they -lrb- sidenote : ad 63 -lrb- au 816 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 15 -- -rrb- indeed when many of those who have gather at antium perish nero make that too a occasion for a festival a certain thrasea give he opinion to the effect that for a senator the extreme penalty should be exile -lrb- sidenote : ad 64 -lrb- au 817 -rrb- -rrb- to such length do nero 's self-indulgence go that he actually drive chariot in public again one time after the slaughter of beast he straightway bring water into the theater by means of pipe and produce a sea-fight : then he let the water out again and arrange a gladiatorial combat last of all he flood the place once more and give a costly public banquet the person who have be appoint director of the banquet be tigillinus and a large and complete equipment have be furnish the arrangement make be as follow in the center and rest on the water be place the great wooden wine vessel over which board have be fasten round about it have be build tavern and booth thus nero and tigillinus and they fellow-banqueter be in the center hold they feast on purple carpet and soft mattress while all the other people carouse in the tavern these also enter the brothel where unrestrictedly they might enjoy absolutely any woman to be find there now the latter be some of the most beautiful and distinguish in the city both slave and free some hetaerae some virgin some wife -- not merely that be to say public wench but both girl and woman of the very noblest family every man be give authority to have whichever one he wish for the woman be not allow to refuse any one consequently the multitude be a regular rabble they drink greedily and revel in wanton conduct so a slave debauch he mistress in the presence of he master and a gladiator ravish a girl of noble family while she father look on the shove and striking and uproar that go on first on the part of those who be go in and second on the part of those who stand around outside be disgraceful many man meet they death in these encounter and of the woman some be strangle and some be seize and carry off -lrb- sidenote : -- 16 -- -rrb- after this nero have the wish -lrb- or rather it have always be a fixed purpose of he -rrb- to make a end of the whole city and sovereignty during he lifetime priam he deem wonderfully happy in that he have see he country perish at the same moment as he authority accordingly he send in different direction man feign to be drunk or engage in some indifferent species of rascality and at first have one or two or more blaze quietly kindle in different quarter : people of course fall into the utmost confusion not be able to find any beginning of the trouble nor to put any end to it and meanwhile they become aware of many strange sight and sound for soon there be nothing to be observe but many fire as in a camp and no other phrase fall from man 's lip but this or that be burn where how who set it to the rescue a extraordinary perturbation lay hold on all wherever they might be and they run about as if distract some in one direction and some in another some man in the midst of assist they neighbor would learn that they own premise be on fire other receive the first intimation of they own possession be aflame when inform that they be destroy person would run from they house into the lane with some idea of be of assistance from the outside or again they would dash into the dwelling from the street appear to think they could accomplish something inside the shouting and scream of child woman man and graybeard all together be incessant so that one could have no consciousness nor comprehension of anything by reason of the smoke and shout combine on this account some might be see stand speechless as if dumb all this time many who be carry out they goods and many more who be steal what belong to other keep encounter one another and fall over the merchandise it be not possible to get anywhere nor yet to stand still but people push and be push back they upset other and be themselves upset many be suffocate many be crush : in fine no evil that can possibly happen to man at such a crisis fail to befall they they could not with ease find even any avenue of escape and if any one do save himself from some immediate danger he usually fall into another one and be lose -lrb- sidenote : -- 17 -- -rrb- this do not all take place on one day but last for several day and night together many house be destroy through lack of some one to defend they and many be set on fire in still more place by person who presumably come to the rescue for the soldier -lrb- include the night watch -rrb- have a eye upon plunder instead of extinguish any blaze kindle greater conflagration while similar scene be be enact at various point a sudden wind catch the fire and sweep it over whatever remain consequently no one concerned himself any longer about goods or house but all the survivor stand in a place of safety gaze upon what seem to be many island and city burn there be no longer any grief over individual loss for it be swallow up in the public lamentation as man remind one another how once before most of they city have be similarly lay waste by the gaul -lrb- sidenote : -- 18 -- -rrb- while the whole population be in this state of mind and many craze by the disaster be leap into the blaze itself nero mount to the roof of the palace where nearly the whole conflagration could be take in by a sweeping glance and have assume the lyrist 's garb he sing the taking -lrb- as he say -rrb- of ilium which to the ordinary vision however appear to be the taking of rome the calamity which the city at this time experience have no parallel before or since except in the gallic invasion the whole palatine hill the theater of taurus and nearly two-third of the remainder of the city be burn and countless human being perish the populace invoke curse upon nero without intermission not utter he name but simply cursing those who have set the city on fire : and this be especially the case because they be disturb by the memory of the oracle chant in tiberius 's day these be the word : -- thrice three hundred cycle of tireless year be end civil strife shall the roman destroy -lrb- footnote : compare book fifty-seven chapter 18 -rrb- and when nero by way of encourage they report that these verse be nowhere to be find they change and go to repeat another oracle which they aver to be a genuine sibylline production namely : -- last of the son of aenea a matricide shall govern and so it prove whether this be actually reveal beforehand by some divination or whether the populace now for the first time give it the form of a divine say adapt to exist circumstance for nero be indeed the last emperor of the julian line descend from aenea he now begin to collect vast sum from both individual and nation sometimes use compulsion with the conflagration for he excuse and sometimes obtain it by voluntary offer and the mass of the roman have the food supply fund withdraw -lrb- sidenote : -- 19 -- -rrb- while he be so engage he receive news from armenia and soon after a laurel wreath in honor of victory the scatter body of soldiery in that region have be unite by corbulo who train they sedulously after a period of neglect and then by the very report of he come have terrify both vologaesus king of parthium and tiridate chief of armenia he resemble the primitive roman in that besides come of a brilliant family and besides possess much strength of body he be still further gifted with a shrewd intelligence : and he behave with great bravery with great fairness and with great good faith toward all both friend and enemy for these reason nero have despatch he to the scene of war in he own stead and have entrust to he a larger force than to anybody else be equally assure that the man would subdue the barbarian and would not revolt against he and corbulo prove neither of these assumption false all other man however have it as a particular grievance against he that he keep faith with nero they be very anxious to get he as emperor in place of the actual despot and this conduct of he seem to they he only defect -lrb- sidenote : -- 20 -- -rrb- corbulo accordingly have take artaxa without a struggle and have raze the city to the ground this exploit finish he march in the direction of tigranocerta spare all the district that yield themselves but devastate the land of all such as resist he tigranocerta submit to he voluntarily and he perform other brilliant and glorious deed as a result of which he induce the formidable vologaesus to accept term that accord with the roman reputation -lrb- for vologaesus on hearing that nero have assign armenia to other and that adiabene be be ravage by tigrane make preparation himself to go on a campaign into syrium against corbulo but send into armenia monobazus king of adiabene and monaese a parthian these two have shut up tigrane in tigranocerta but since they do not succeed in harm he at all by they siege and as often as they try conclusion with he be repulse by both the native troops and the roman that be in he army and since corbulo guard syrium with extreme care vologaesus recognize the hopelessness of he attempt and disband he force then he send to corbulo and obtain peace on condition that he send a new embassy to nero raise the siege and withdraw he soldier from armenia nero make he no immediate nor speedy nor definite reply but despatch lucius caesennius paetus to cappadocium to see to it that there should be no armenian uprising -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 21 -- -rrb- -lrb- so vologaesus attack tigranocerta and drive back paetus who have come to its aid when the latter flee he pursue he beat back the garrison leave by paetus at the taurus and shut he up in rhandea near the river arsania then he be on the point of retire without accomplish anything for destitute as he be of heavy-armed soldier he could not approach close to the wall and he have no large stock of provender particularly as he have come at the head of a vast host without make arrangement for food supplies paetus however stand in terror of he archery which take effect in the very camp itself as well as of the cavalry which keep appear at all point hence he make peace proposal to he antagonist accept he term and take a oath that he would himself abandon all of armenia and that nero should give it to tiridate the parthian be satisfy enough with this agreement see that he be to obtain control of the country without a contest and would be make the roman he debtor for a very considerable kindness and as he learn that corbulo -lrb- whom paetus several time send for before he be surround -rrb- be draw near he dismiss the beleaguered soldier have first make they agree previous knowledge of what should come to pass -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- vitellius be fond of luxury and licentiousness and care for nothing else human or divine he have always be the kind of man side then to the other now of one kind of fight force now of another infantry or cavalry : and the conflict be mark by vicissitude until all have hasten to the front then they get into some kind of amount himself -lrb- sidenote : -- 3 -- -rrb- in germany various uprising against the roman take place which be not worth mention for my purpose but there be one incident that must cause we surprise a grow hollow from continual collapse thus the entire mountain if we may compare great thing to small resemble a hunting-theatre the outlying height of it support both tree and vine -- many of they -- but the crater be give over to fire and send up smoke by day flame by night it look as if quantity of incense of all sort be be burn in it this go on all the time sometimes more sometimes less often it throw up ash when there be a general settling in the interior or again it send up stone when the air force they out it echo and bellows too because its vent be not all together but be narrow and befall number of huge man quite surpass any human stature -- such creature as giant be depict to be -- appear now on the mountain now in the country surround it and again in the city wander over the earth day and night and also traverse the air after this fearful drought and earthquake sudden and violent occur so that all the level ground in that region undulated and the height give a great leap reverberation be frequent some subterranean resemble thunder and some on the surface like bellowing the sea join the roar and the sky resound with it then suddenly a portentous crash be hear as if the mountain be tumble in ruin and first there be belch forth stone of huge size that rise to the very summit before they fall after they come a deal of fire and smoke in inexhaustible quantity so that the whole atmosphere be obscure and the whole sun be screen from view as if in a eclipse -lrb- sidenote : -- 23 -- -rrb- thus night succeed day and darkness light some think the giant be rise in revolt -lrb- for even at this time many of they form could be discern in the smoke and moreover a kind of sound of trumpet be hear -rrb- while other believe that the whole world be disappear in chaos or fire therefore they flee some from the house into the street other from without into the house in they confusion indeed they hasten from the sea to the land or from the land to the sea deem any place at a distance from where they be safer than what be near by while this be go on a inconceivable amount of ash be blow out and cover the land and the sea everywhere and fill all the air it do harm of all sort as chance dictate to man and place and cattle and the fish and the bird it utterly destroy moreover it bury two whole city herculaneum and pompeius while the populace be seat in the theater the entire amount of dust be so great that some of it reach africa and syrium and egypt and it also enter rome where it occupy all the air over the city and cast the sun into shadow there too no little fear be feel for several day since the people do not know and could not conjecture what have happen they like the rest think that everything be be turn upside down that the sun be disappear in the earth and the earth be bound up to the sky this ash for the time be do they no great harm : later it breed among they a terrible pestilence -lrb- sidenote : ad 80 -lrb- au 833 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 24 -- -rrb- another fire above ground in the following year spread over a very large portion of rome while titus be absent on business connect with the catastrophe that have befall in campanium it consume the temple of serapi the temple of isis the saepta the temple of neptune the bath of agrippa the pantheon the diribitorium the theater of balbus the stage-building of pompey 's theater the octavian building together with they book and the temple of capitoline jupiter with its surround temple hence the disaster seem to be not of human but of divine contrivance any one can estimate from the list of building that i have give how many more must have be destroy titus accordingly send two exconsul to the campanian to supervise the founding of settlement and bestow upon the inhabitant money that come -lrb- besides various other source -rrb- from those citizen that have die without heir as for himself he take nothing from individual or city or king although many keep -lrb- ad 96 = au 849 = sixteenth of domitian to sept 18th -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 81 -lrb- au 834 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 1 -- -rrb- domitian be both bold and passionate both treacherous and give to dissemble hence from these two characteristic rashness on the one hand and craftiness on the other he do much harm fall upon some person with the swiftness of a thunderbolt and damaging other by carefully prepared plot the divinity that he chiefly revere be minerva so that he be wont to celebrate the panathenaea on a magnificent scale : on this occasion he have contest of poet and chronicler and gladiator almost every year at albanum this district situate below the alban mount from which it be name he have set apart as a kind of acropoli he have no genuine affection for any human be save a few woman but he always pretend to love the person whom at any time he be most determine to slay he could not be rely upon even by those who do he some favor or help he in he most revolting crime for whenever any person furnish he with large sum of money or lodge information against number of man he be sure to destroy these benefactor be especially careful to do so in the case of slave who have give information against they master -lrb- accordingly such individual though they receive money and honor and office all at once from he live in no greater honor and security than other man the very offence to which they have -lrb- sidenote : ad 82 -lrb- au 835 -rrb- -rrb- be urge by domitian commonly be make pretext for they destruction the emperor 's object be to have the actual perpetrator appear solely responsible for they wrongdoing it be the same intention which lead he once to issue a public notice to the effect that when a emperor do not punish informer he be the cause of the existence of such a class -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- though this be he behavior to all throughout the course of he reign still he quite outdo himself in deal dishonor and ruin to he father 's and brother 's friend -lrb- to be sure he himself post a notice that he would ratify all the gift make to any person by they and by other emperor but this be mere show -rrb- he hate they because they do not supply all he demand many of which be unreasonable as also because they have be hold in some honor -lrb- whatever have enjoy they affection and the benefit of they influence beyond the ordinary he regard as hostile to he -rrb- therefore although he himself have a passion for a eunuch name earinus nevertheless because titus have also show great liking for castrated person he carry he desire to cast reflection on he brother 's character to the extent of forbid any one thereafter in the roman empire to be castrate in general he be accustom to say that those emperor who fail to punish large number of man be not good but merely fortunate -lrb- personally he pay no attention to those who praise titus for not cause a single senator 's death nor do he care that the senate frequently see fit to pass decree that the emperor should not be permit to put to death any of he peer the emperor as he believe be far and away superior to they and might put any one of they out of the way either on he own responsibility or with the consent of the rest it be ridiculous to suppose that they could offer any opposition or refuse to condemn a man some would praise titus only not in domitian 's hearing for such effrontery would be deem as grave a offence as if they be to revile the emperor in he presence and within hearing : but -lrb- lacuna -rrb- -lrb- footnote : a gap somebody 's litter and sometimes he would enter person ' house even without a guard and make himself at home he lack education in the exact sense -- book-learning at least -- but he both understand result of this he would have incur censure as the case stand he drink all the wine he want yet remain sober and he pursuit of pederasty harm no one and even if he do delight in war still he be satisfy one hundred and seventy foot from one to another be connect by arch how then could one fail to be astonish at the expenditure make upon they or the manner in which each of they be place in a river so deep in water so full of eddy on ground so slimy it be impossible you note to divert the course of the river in any direction i have speak of the breadth of the river but the stream be not uniformly so limited since it cover in some place twice and elsewhere thrice as much ground but the narrowest point and the one in that region most adapt to bridge-building have just those dimension yet the very fact that the river here shrink from a great flood to such a narrow channel and be here confine though it again expand into a greater flood make it all the more violent and deep and this feature must be consider in estimate the difficulty of prepare a bridge this achievement then show the greatness of trajan 's design though the bridge be of no particular use to we merely the pier be stand afford no means of cross as if they be erect for the sole purpose of demonstrate that there be nothing which human energy can not accomplish trajan 's reason for construct the bridge be he fear that some time when the ister be frozen war might be make on the roman across the water and he desire to enjoy the easy access to they that this work would permit hadrian on the contrary be afraid that the barbarian might overpower the guard at the bridge and cross into moesium and so he remove the surface work -lrb- sidenote : ad 105 -lrb- au 858 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 14 -- -rrb- trajan have cross the ister on this bridge conduct the war with prudence rather than with haste and eventually after a hard struggle vanquish the dacian in the course of these encounter he personally perform many deed of good generalship and bravery and he soldier run many risk and display great prowess on he behalf it be here that a certain horseman dangerously wound be carry from the battle on the supposition that he could be heal but when he find that he could not recover he rush from he quarter -lrb- since he hurt have not incapacitate he -rrb- and station himself in the line again he perish after have display great valor -lrb- sidenote : ad 106 -lrb- au 859 -rrb- -rrb- decebalus when he capital and all he territory have be occupy and he be himself in danger of be capture committed suicide and he head be bring to rome in this way dacium become subject to rome and trajan found city there the treasure of decebalus be also discover though hidden beneath the sargetium river which run past he palace he have make some captive divert the course of the river and have then excavate its bed there he have place a large amount of silver and of gold and other object of great value that could endure some moisture have heap stone over they and pile on earth after that he have let the river flow over they the same captive be compel to deposit he robe and other similar object in neighbor cave and when he have effect this he make away with they to prevent they talking but bicili a comrade of he who know what have be do be seize and give this information -- about this same time palma who be governor of syrium subdue the portion of arabium near petra and make it subservient to the roman -lrb- sidenote : -- 15 -- -rrb- -lrb- the ambassador who come from the king be give seat by trajan in the senatorial row at spectacles -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 107 -lrb- au 860 -rrb- -rrb- upon trajan 's return to rome the greatest imaginable number of embassy come to he from the barbarian even the indus be represent and he give spectacles on one hundred and twenty-three day at these affair thousand yes possibly ten of thousand of animal both wild and tame be slaughter and fully ten thousand gladiator fight in combat about the same period he make the pontine marsh traversable by means of a stone foundation and build road alongside which he furnish with most magnificent bridge -- all the obsolete money he have melt down -lrb- he have swear not to commit bloodshed and he confirm he promise by he action in spite of plot he be by nature not at all give to duplicity or guile or harshness he love and greet and honor the good and the rest he neglect he age make he still more inclined to mildness -rrb- when licinius sura die he bestow upon he a public funeral and a statue this man have attain such a degree of wealth and pride that he build a gymnasium for the roman so great be the friendship and confidence -lrb- which sura show toward trajan and trajan toward he that although the man be often slander -- as naturally happen in the case of all those who possess any influence with the emperor -- trajan never feel a moment 's suspicion or hatred on the contrary when those who envy he become insistent trajan -rrb- go -lrb- uninvited to he house -rrb- to dinner and have dismiss he whole body-guard he first call sura 's physician and have he anoint he eye and then he barber shave he chin anciently the emperor themselves as well as all other people use to do this it be hadrian who first set the fashion of wear a beard when he have do this he next take a bath and have dinner so the next day he say to he friend who be always in the habit of make statement detrimental to sura : if sura have want to kill I he would have kill I yesterday -lrb- sidenote : -- 16 -- -rrb- now he do a great thing in run this risk in the case of a man who have be calumniate but a still greater thing in believe that he would never be harm by he so it be that the confidence of he mind be strengthen by he own knowledge of he dealings with sura instead of be influence by the fancy of other indeed when he first hand to he -lrb- footnote : saburanus -lrb- -rrb- -rrb- who be to be prefect of the pretorian the sword which the latter require to wear by he side he bare the blade hold it up say : take this sword to the end that if i rule well you may use it for I but if ill against I he also set up image of sosium and palma and celsus -lrb- footnote : _ l publilius celsus _ -rrb- -- so greatly do he esteem they above other those however who conspire against he -lrb- among whom be crassus -rrb- he bring before the senate and cause to be punish -lrb- sidenote : ad 114 -lrb- au 867 -rrb- -rrb- again he gather collection of book and he set up in the forum a enormous column to serve at once as a sepulchral monument to himself and as a reminder of he work in the forum the whole region there be hilly and he dig it down for a distance equal the height of the column thus make the forum level -lrb- sidenote : -- 17 -- -rrb- next he make a campaign against the armenian and parthian on the pretext that the armenian king -lrb- footnote : _ exedare _ -rrb- have obtain he diadem not at he hand but from the parthian king -lrb- footnote : _ osrho _ -rrb- he real reason however be a desire to win fame -lrb- on he campaign against the parthian when he have reach athen a embassy from osrho meet he ask for peace and proffer gift this king have learn of he advance and be terrify because trajan be wont to make good he threat by deed therefore he humble he pride and send a supplication that war be not make against he : he ask armenia for parthomasiri who be likewise a son of pacorus and request that the diadem be send to he he have put a stop he say to the reign of exedare who be beneficial neither to the roman nor to the parthian the emperor neither receive the gift nor send any answer or command save that friendship be determine by deed and not by word and that accordingly when he should reach syrium he would do what be proper and be of this mind he proceed through asia syrium and adjoining province to seleucium upon he come to antioch abgarus the osrhoenian do not appear in person but send gift and a friendly communication for as he dread both he and the parthian he be try to play a double game and for that reason would not come to confer with he -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 19 -- -rrb- parthomasiri behave in rather violent fashion in he first letter to trajan he have sign himself as king but when no answer come to he epistle he write again omit this title and ask that marcus junius the governor of cappadocium be send to he imply that he want to prefer some request through he trajan accordingly send he the son of junius and himself go ahead to arsamosa of which he take possession without a struggle then he come to satalum and reward with gift anchialus the king of the heniochus and machelone at elegeium in armenia he await parthomasiri he be seat upon a platform in the trench the prince greet he take off he diadem from he head and lay it at he foot then he stand there in silence expect to receive it back at this the soldier shout aloud and hail trajan imperator as if on account of some victory -lrb- they term it a uncrowned -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- greek : haselinon -rrb- -lrb- bekker -rrb- = without the parsley crown -lrb- such as be bestow upon victor in some of the greek game -rrb- -rrb- bloodless victory to see the king a descendant of arsace a son of pacorus and a nephew of osrho stand beside trajan without a diadem like a captive -rrb- the shout terrify the prince who think that it herald insult and destruction for he he turn about as if to flee but see that he be hem in on all side beg as a favor not to be oblige to speak before the crowd accordingly he be escort into the tent where he have none of he wish grant -lrb- sidenote : -- 20 -- -rrb- so out he rush in a rage and from there out of the camp but trajan send for he and again ascend the platform bid he speak in the hearing of all everything that he desire this be to prevent any person from spread a false report through ignorance of what have be say in private conference on hearing this exhortation parthomasiri no longer keep silence but with great frankness make many statement some of they be to the effect that he have not be defeat or capture but have come there voluntarily believe that he should not be wrong and should receive back the kingdom as tiridate have receive it from nero trajan make appropriate reply to all he remark and say that he should abandon armenia to no one it belong to the roman and should have a roman governor he would however allow parthomasiri to depart to any place he please so he send the prince away together with he parthian companion and give they a escort of cavalry to ensure they meeting no one and adopt no rebellious tactic all the armenian who have come with he he command to remain where they be on the ground that they be already he subject -lrb- sidenote : -- 21 -- -rrb- -lrb- leave garrison at opportune point trajan come to edessa and there for the first time he set eye upon abgarus previously this person have send envoy and gift to the prince frequently but he himself for different reason at different time fail to put in a appearance the same be true also of mannus the phylarch of adjoining arabium and sporace phylarch of anthemusium on this occasion however he be persuade partly by he son arvande who be beautiful and in the prime of youth and therefore on good term with trajan and partly by the fear of the latter 's presence near by consequently he meet he on the road make he apology and obtain pardon he have a powerful intercessor in the boy accordingly he become a friend of trajan 's and entertain he with a banquet at the dinner in question he present he boy in some kind of barbaric dance -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 22 -- -rrb- -lrb- when trajan come into mesopotamium mannus send a herald to he and manisarus despatch envoy in regard to peace because he say osrho be make a campaign against he and he be ready to withdraw from armenia and mesopotamium so far as capture thereupon the emperor reply that he would not believe he until he should come to he and confirm he offer by deed as he be promise he be also suspicious of mannus especially because the latter have send a auxiliary force to mebarsape king of adiabene and then have lose it all at the hand of the roman therefore mannus never wait for the roman to draw near but take he course to adiabene to find shelter with the other two prince thus be singara and some other point occupy by lusius without a battle -rrb- when he have capture the whole country of armenia and have win over also many of the king some of whom since they submit he treat as he friend and other though disobedient he subdue without resort to arm -lrb- sidenote : -- 23 -- -rrb- the senate false report in order that the soldier might at the same time practice military maneuver and be so impervious to alarm as to be ready for anything after he have capture nisibi and batnae he be give the title of parthicus but he take greater pride in the name of optimus than in all the rest inasmuch as it belong rather to he character than to he arm -lrb- sidenote : ad 115 -lrb- au 868 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 24 -- -rrb- while he be stay in antioch a dreadful earthquake occur many city be damage but antioch be most of all unfortunate since trajan be winter there and many soldier and many private person have flock thither from all direction for lawsuit embassy business or sightseeing there be no nation nor people that go unscathed thus in antioch the whole world under roman sway suffer disaster there be many thunderstorm to start with and portentous wind but no one could have expect that so many evil would result from they first come on a sudden a great bellow roar and there follow it a tremendous shock the whole earth be up-heaved and building leap into the air those that be lift up collapse and be smash to piece -lrb- sidenote : ad 115 -lrb- au 868 -rrb- -rrb- while other be beat this way and that as if by the surge and be turn about the wreck be strew a long distance over the countryside the crash of grind and break timber tile and stone together become most frightful and a inconceivable mass of dust arise so that no one could see any person nor say or hear anything many person be hurt even outside the house be pick up and toss violently about and then with a momentum as in a fall from a cliff dash to the earth some be maim other kill not a few tree leap into the air root and all the number of those find in the house who perish be beyond discovery multitude be destroy by the very force of the collapse and crowd be suffocate in the debris those who lay with a part of they body bury under the stone or timber suffer fearful agony be able neither to live nor to find a immediate death -lrb- sidenote : -- 25 -- -rrb- nevertheless many even of these be save as be natural in such overwhelming number of people and those outside do not all get off safe and sound number lose they leg or they shoulder and some -lrb- lacuna -rrb- they -lrb- lacuna -rrb- head other vomit blood one of these be pedo the consul and he die at once in brief there be no form of violent experience that those people do not undergo at that time and as heaven continue the earthquake for several day and night the people be dismayed and helpless some crushed and perish under the weight of the building press upon they and other die of hunger in case it chance that by the inclination of the timber they be leave alive in a clear space it might be in a kind of arch-shaped colonnade when at last the trouble have subside some one who venture to mount the ruin catch sight of a live woman she be not alone but have also a infant and have endure by feed both herself and she child with she milk they dig she out and resuscitate she together with she offspring and after that they search the other heap but be no longer able to find in they any live creature save a child suck at the breast of its mother who be dead as they draw out the corpse they no longer feel any pleasure at they own escape so great be the disaster that have overwhelm antioch at this time trajan make he way out through a window of the room where he be some being of more than human stature have approach he and lead he forth so that he survive with only a few small bruise as the shock extend over a number of day he live out of door in the hippodrome casium itself too be so shake that its peak seem to bend and break and to be fall upon the city other hill settle and quantity of water not previously in existence come to light while quantity more escape by flow away -lrb- sidenote : -- 26 -- -rrb- trajan about spring time proceed into the enemy 's country now since the region near the tigri be barren of timber fit for shipbuilding he bring the boat which have be construct in the forest surround nisibi on wagon to the river the vessel have be arrange in such a way that they could be take apart and put together he have very hard work in bridge the stream opposite mount carduenum for the oppose barbarian try to hinder he trajan however have a great abundance of both ship and soldier and so some boat be fasten together with great speed while other lay motionless in front of they carry heavy infantry and archer still other keep make dash this way and that as if they intend to cross as a result of these tactic and from they very astonishment at see so many ship at once appear _ en masse _ from a land devoid of tree the barbarian give way and the roman cross over they win possession of the whole of adiabene -lrb- this be a portion of assyrium in the vicinity of ninus and arbelum and gaugamelum close to which alexander conquer darius be also in this same territory the country have also be call atyrium in the language of the barbarian the double s be change to t -rrb- -lrb- adenystra be a strong post to which one sentius a centurion have be send as a envoy to mebarsape he be imprison by the latter in that place and later at the approach of the roman he make a arrangement with some of he fellow-prisoner and with they aid escape from he shackle kill the commander of the garrison and open the gate to he countryman -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 26 -- -rrb- hereupon they advance as far as babylon itself be quite free from molestation since the parthian power have be ruin by civil conflict and be still at this time involve in dissension -lrb- sidenote : -- 27 -- -rrb- cassius dio cocceianus in writings concern the latin have write that this city -lrb- ie babylon -rrb- comprise a circuit of four hundred stade -lrb- compare also tzetz exegesis of homer 's iliad p 141 15 ff -rrb- here moreover trajan see the asphalt out of which the wall of babylon have be build when mix with baked brick or smooth stone this material afford so great strength as to render they stronger than rock or any kind of iron he also look at the opening from which issue a deadly vapor that destroy any creature living upon the earth and any winged thing that so much as inhale a breath of it if it extend far above ground or have several vent the place would not be inhabitable but as it be this gas circle round within itself and remain stationary hence creature that fly high enough above it and such as remain to one side be safe i see another open like it at hierapoli in asia and test it by means of bird i bent over it myself and myself gaze down upon the vapor it be enclose in a sort of a cistern and a theater have be build over it it destroy all live thing save human being that have be emasculate the reason for that i can not comprehend i relate what i have see as i have see it and what i have hear as i have hear it -lrb- sidenote : ad 116 -lrb- au 869 -rrb- -rrb- trajan have plan to conduct the euphrate through a channel into the tigri in order that boat might be float down by this route afford he a opportunity to make a bridge but on learn facilitate by he proximity and he have a large force under he command my father apronianus who be governor of cilicium have ascertain accurately the whole story about he he use to relate the different be not he but plotina 's she have not do this in any previous instance -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- at the time that he be declare emperor hadrian be in antioch the metropolis of syrium of which he be governor in a dream just before that day he seem to see fire descend from heaven in the midst of clear sky and wholly fair weather and fall first upon the left of he throat and then upon the right also though it neither frightened nor injured he and hadrian write to the senate ask that he sovereignty be confirm also by that body and forbid any measure to be vote -lrb- as be so often do -rrb- either then or thereafter that contain any special honor for he unless he should first himself approve it the bone of trajan be deposit in he column and the so-called parthian game continue for a for other and swear that he will neither do anything contrary to the public advantage nor put to death any senator call down destruction upon himself if he shall transgress these principle in any way enrol among the hero those murder at the beginning be palma and celsus nigrinus and lusius the first two for the alleged reason that they have conspire against he during a hunt and the other on certain other complaint because they have great influence or be in a strong position as regard wealth and fame hadrian feel so keenly the talk that be make about they that he defend himself and declare upon oath that he have not order they death those that perish at the end of the reign be servianus and he grandson fuscus hadrian be a pleasant man to meet and he presence shed a kind of grace -lrb- sidenote : -- 3 -- -rrb- as for hadrian 's family he be a son of -lrb- a man of senatorial rank a ex-praetor -rrb- hadrianus -lrb- for thus he be name -rrb- in regard to he disposition he be fond of literature in both language and have leave behind all kind of prose piece as well as composition in verse he ambition be insatiable and as a result he practice all conceivable pursuit even the most trivial he model and paint and declare that there be nothing in peace or in war in imperial or in private life of which he be not cognizant -lrb- and this of course do people no harm but he jealousy of those who excel in any branch be terrible and -rrb- ruin many besides utterly destroy quite a few -lrb- for -rrb- since he desire to surpass everybody in everything -lrb- he hate those who attain eminence in any direction -rrb- this feeling it be which lead he to undertake the overthrow of two sophist favorinus the gaul and dionysius the milesian -lrb- by various method chiefly -rrb- by stir up they antagonist -lrb- who be of little or no worth at all -rrb- dionysius be say to have remark at this time to avidius -lrb- footnote : boissevain 's reading -rrb- heliodorus who manage he correspondence : caesar can give you money and honor but he can not make you a orator favorinus be about to bring a case before the emperor in regard to exemption from tax a privilege which he desire to secure in he native city suspect however that he should be unsuccessful and be insult in addition he enter the courtroom to be sure but make no other statement save : my teacher stand this night in a dream by my side and bid I do service for my country since i have be bear in it -lrb- sidenote : -- 4 -- -rrb- now hadrian spare these man although he be displeased with they for he could find no satisfactory pretext to use against they that might compass they destruction but he first banish and later actually put to death apollodorus the architect who have plan the various creation of trajan in rome -- the forum the odeum and the gymnasium the excuse give be that he have be guilty of some misdemeanor but the true reason be that when trajan be consult he on some point about the work he have say to hadrian who break in with some remark : be off and draw gourd you do not understand any of these matter it happen that hadrian at the time be plume himself upon some such drawing when he -rrb- these act be charge against he as offence and so be also he great exactness he superfluous labor and he divide interest but he heal the wound make and recover favor by he general care he foresight he grandeur and he skill again he do not stir up any war and end those already in progress he deprive no one of money unjustly and upon many people and private citizen and senator and knight he bestow large sum he do not wait to be ask but be certain to act each time accord to each man 's need the military he train with great precision so that its strength render it neither disobedient nor insolent ally and subject city he aid most munificently he have see many that no other emperor have even set eye upon and he assist practically all of they give to some water to other harbor or food or public work or money and to still other various honor -lrb- sidenote : -- 6 -- -rrb- as a leader of the roman people he be distinguish for force rather than for flattery once at a gladiatorial unexpected way and by chance comer it must be admit that once when a woman pass he on some road and prefer a request he at first say to she : i have not time afterwards when she cry out loudly say : do not be emperor then he turn about and grant she a hearing -lrb- sidenote : -- 7 -- -rrb- he transact through the senate all serious and most urgent business and he hold court with the assistance of prominent man now in the palace or again in the forum the pantheon and in many other place always on a platform so that what be do be open to public inspection sometimes he would join the consul when _ they _ be try case and he show they honor at the horse-race when he return home he be accustom to be carry in a litter in order not to trouble any one to accompany he on day neither sacred nor public he remain at home and admit no one even long enough to greet he unless it be some urgent matter this be to relieve the courtier of needless annoyance both in rome and abroad he always keep the noblest man about he and he use to join they at banquet which lead to he be often carry in they litter as one of a party of four as frequently as possible he go hunting and he breakfast without wine in fact most of he food be serve without any accompany beverage and often in the midst of a meal he would turn he attention to a case at law : later he would drive in the company of all the foremost and best man and they eating together be the occasion for all kind of discussion when he friend be very ill he would go to see they and he use to attend they festival besides evince pleasure at visit they country seat and house as might have be expect then he set up in he forum image for many who be dead and many still alive no one of he associate moreover display insolence nor sell aught that he should pronounce or perform as the caesarian and other attendant in the suite of emperor have make it they custom to do -lrb- sidenote : -- 8 -- -rrb- this be a kind of preface of a summary nature i hadrian rebuke they so true it be that a emperor 's word have more power than force of arm -lrb- sidenote : ad 118 -lrb- au 871 -rrb- -rrb- on come to rome he cancel debt owe to the imperial treasury
