own choosing and hadrian assent to he drinking hemlock in consideration of he extreme age and sickliness -lrb- sidenote : -- 9 -- -rrb- hadrian go from one province to another visit the district and city and observe all the garrison and fortification some of these he remove to more desirable location some he abolish and he found some new one he personally oversee and investigate absolutely everything not merely the usual appurtenance of camp -- i mean weapon and engine and ditch and enclosure and palisade -- but also the private affair of each one and the life the dwelling and the character both of the man serve in the organization and of the commander themselves many case of too delicate living and equipment he harmonize with military need and reform in various way he exercise the man in every variety of battle honor some and reprove other he teach all of they what they ought to do and to make sure that they should obtain benefit from observe _ he _ he lead everywhere a severe existence and walk or ride horseback on all occasion never at this period do he enter either a chariot or a four-wheeled vehicle he cover he head neither in heat nor in cold but alike in celtic snow and under scorch egyptian sun he go about with it bare -lrb- sidenote : ad 119 -lrb- au 872 -rrb- -rrb- in fine so thoroughly by action and exhortation do he train and discipline the whole antoninus to march 7th -rrb- i from dio : -lrb- sidenote : ad 138 -lrb- au 891 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 1 -- -rrb- it should be note that information about antoninus pius be not find in the copy of dio probably because the book have meet with some accident so that the history of he reign be almost wholly unknown save that when lucius commodus whom hadrian have adopt die before hadrian antoninus be also adopt by he and become emperor and that when the senate demur to give heroic honor to hadrian after he demise on account of certain murder of eminent man antoninus address many word to they with tear and lament and finally say : i will not govern you either if he have become base and inimical and a national foe in you eye for you will of course be annul all he act of which my adoption be one on hearing this the senate both through respect for the man and through a certain fear of the soldier bestow the honor upon hadrian -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- only this in regard to antoninus be preserve in dio yes one thing more -- that the senate give he the title both of augustus and of pius for some such reason as the follow when in the beginning of he imperial reign many man be accuse and some of they have be intercede for by name he nevertheless punish no one say : i must not begin my career of supervision with such deed -lrb- sidenote : lxix 15 3 -rrb- -lrb- when pharasmane the iberian come to rome with he wife he increase he domain allow he to offer sacrifice on the capitoline set up a statue of he on horseback in the temple of bellona and view a exercise in arm of the chieftain he son and the other prominent iberian -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 139 -lrb- au 892 -rrb- -rrb- we do not find preserved either the first part of the account of marcus verus who rule after antoninus and all that the latter himself do in the case of lucius son of commodus whom marcus make he son-in-law and all that lucius accomplish when send by he father to the war against vologaesus i shall speak briefly about these matter gather my material from other book and then i shall go back to the continuation of dio 's narrative ii from xiphilinus : -lrb- sidenote : lxx 3 -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 153 -lrb- au 906 -rrb- -rrb- antoninus be admit by all to have be noble and good not oppressive to the christian nor severe to any of he other subject instead he show the christian great respect and add to the honor in which hadrian have be wont to hold they for eusebius son of pamphilus cite in he church history -lrb- footnote : iv 9 -rrb- some letter of hadrian in which the latter be show to threaten terrible vengeance upon those who harm in any way or accuse the christian and to swear by hercule that they shall receive punishment antoninus be say also to have be of a enquire turn of mind and not to have hold aloof from careful investigation of even small and commonplace matter for this those dispose to scoff call he cumminsplitter -lrb- sidenote : ad 161 -lrb- au 914 -rrb- -rrb- quadratus state that he die at a advanced age and that the happiest death befall he like unto gentlest slumber -lrb- sidenote : -lrb- ad 177 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 4 -- -rrb- in the day of antoninus also a most frightful earthquake be say to have occur in the region of bithynium and the hellespont various city be severely damage or fall without a building leave standing and in particular cyzicus and the temple there that be the greatest and most beautiful of all temple be throw down its column be four cubit in thickness and fifty cubit in height each of a single block of stone and each of the other feature of the edifice be more to be wonder at than to be praise somewhere in the interior of the country the peak of a mountain rise upward and surge of the sea be say to have gush out while the spray from pure transparent sea-water be drive to a great distance over the land -lrb- footnote : compare also zonaras v 12 -lrb- p 80 ii 3-11 dind -rrb- it page 30 ff -lrb- article by de boor -rrb- -rrb- -- so much be the account of antoninus at present extant he reign twenty-four year iii of dio -lrb- or rather of eutropius or john of antioch -rrb- take from the writings of suida this prince antoninus be a excellent man and deserve to be compare especially with numa on account of the similarity of he reign to that king 's just as trajan be see to resemble romulus the private life that antoninus live be thoroughly excellent and honorable -lrb- sidenote : -- 5 -- -rrb- and in he position as ruler he seem to be even more excellent and more prudent to no one be he harsh or oppressive but he be gracious and gentle toward all -lrb- sidenote : -- 6 -- -rrb- in warfare he seek glory rather from a impulse of duty than from one of gain and be determine to preserve the border of the empire intact rather than to extend they to greater distance in the matter of man he appoint to the administration of public affair so far as possible those who be particularly scrupulous about right conduct and he reward good official with the honor that be in he power to grant whereas he banish the worthless -lrb- though without any harshness -rrb- from the conduct of public affair -lrb- sidenote : -- 7 -- -rrb- he be admire not alone by those of he own race but even by foreigner as be show by some of the neighbor barbarian lay down they arm and permit the prince to decide they quarrel by he vote and whereas he have in the course of he life as a private citizen amass a vast amount of money when he enter upon office he expend he own abundance upon gift for the soldier and for he friend to the public treasury he leave a great deal of property of all kind dio 's roman history 71 the emperor marcus take verus as a associate : he give he charge of marcus to march 17th -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 161 -lrb- au 914 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 1 -- -rrb- marcus antoninus the philosopher upon obtain the sovereignty at the death of antoninus who adopt he have immediately take to share the authority with he the son of lucius commodus lucius verus he be personally weak in body and he devote the greater part of he time to letter it be tell that even when he be emperor he show no shame -lrb- or hesitation -rrb- at go to a teacher for instruction but become a pupil of sextus the boeotian philosopher -lrb- footnote : sextus of chaeronea grandson of plutarch -lrb- capitolinus _ vita m antonus philosophi _ 3 2 -rrb- -rrb- and do not hesitate to go to hear the lecture of hermogene on rhetoric he be most inclined to the stoic school lucius on the other hand be strong and rather young and better suit for military enterprise therefore marcus make he he son-in-law by marry he to he daughter lucillum and send he to the parthian war -lrb- sidenote : -- 2 -- -rrb- for vologaesus have begin war by assail on all side the roman camp under severianus situate in elegeium a place in armenia and he have shoot down and destroy the whole force leader and all he be now proceed with number that inspire terror against the city of syrium -lrb- sidenote : ad 162 -lrb- au 915 -rrb- -rrb- lucius accordingly on come to antioch collect a great many soldier and with the best commander under he supervision take up a position in the city spend he time in order all arrangement and in gather the contingent for the war he entrust the army themselves to cassius the latter make a noble stand against the attack -lrb- sidenote : ad 165 -lrb- au 918 -rrb- -rrb- of vologaesus and finally the chieftain be desert by he ally and begin to retire then cassius pursue he as far as seleucium and destroy it and raze to the ground the palace of vologaesus at ctesiphon in the course of he return he lose a great many soldier through famine and disease yet he start off to syria with the man that be leave lucius attain glory by these exploit and feel a just pride in they yet he extreme good fortune do he no good -lrb- sidenote : ad 169 -lrb- au 922 -rrb- -rrb- for he be say to have subsequently plot against he father-in-law marcus and to have perish by poison before he could accomplish anything \* \* \* \* \* fragment of dio from suida -lrb- think by de valois to belong to book lxxi -rrb- -lrb- martius verus send out thucydide to conduct sohaemus into armenia and he in spite of lack of arm apply himself sturdily to this distant task with the inherent good sense that he show in all business fall to he lot marcus have the gift not only of overpower he antagonist or anticipate they by swiftness or outwit they by deceit -lrb- on which quality general most rely -rrb- but also of persuade they by trustworthy promise and conciliate they by generous gift and lure they on by tempting hope he be suave in all that he do or say and soothe the vex and angry feeling of each adversary while greatly raise he hope he know well the right time for flattery and present and entertainment at table and since in addition to these talent he show persistency in endeavor and activity together with speed against he foe he make it plain to the barbarian that he friendship be better worth gain than he enmity so when he arrive at the new city which a garrison of roman place there by priscus be occupy and find they attempt mutiny he take care both by word and by deed to bring they to a better temper and he make the city the foremost of armenia -rrb- -lrb- \* \* _ bridge _ -- by the roman the stream and river be bridge with the greatest ease since the soldier be always practice at it and it be carry on like any other warlike exercise on the ister and the rhine and the euphrate the manner of do it -lrb- which i think not everybody know -rrb- be as follow the boat by means of which the river be bridge be flat they be anchor up stream a little above the spot where the bridge be to be construct when the signal be give they first let one ship drift down stream close to the bank that they be hold when it have come opposite the spot to be bridge they throw into the water a basket fill with stone and fasten with a cord which serve as a anchor make fast in this way the ship be join to the bank by plank and bridgework which the vessel carry in large quantity and immediately a floor be lay to the farther edge then they release another ship at a little distance from this one and another one after that until they run the bridge to the opposite bank the boat which be near the hostile side carry also tower upon it and a gate and archer and catapult as many weapon be hurl at the man engage in bridge cassius order weapon and catapult to be discharge and when the front rank of the barbarian fall the rest give way -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 172 -lrb- au 925 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 3 -- -rrb- cassius however be bid by marcus to have the superintendence of all asia the emperor himself fight for a long time in fact almost he whole life one might say with the barbarian in the ister region the iazyge and the marcomanus first one and then the other and he use pannonium as he start point the langobardus and the obius -lrb- footnote : or perhaps _ osus _ -rrb- to the number of six thousand cross the ister but the cavalry under vindex -lrb- footnote : _ m macrinius avitus catonius vindex _ -rrb- march out and the infantry command by candidus get the start of they so that a utter rout of the barbarian be institute the barbarian throw into consternation by such a outcome of they very first undertaking despatch as envoy to the headquarters of iallius bassus -lrb- footnote : _ m iallius bassus _ -rrb- -lrb- administrator of pannonium -rrb- bellomarius -lrb- footnote : or perhaps _ badomarius _ -rrb- king of the marcomanus and ten more for they select one man per nation the envoy take oath to cement the peace and depart homewards many of the celta too across the rhine advance to the confines of italy and inflict much serious harm upon the roman they in turn be follow up by marcus who oppose to they the lieutenant pompeianus and pertinax pertinax who later become emperor greatly distinguish himself among the corpse of the barbarian be find also the body of woman in armor -lrb- sidenote : ad 168 -lrb- -rrb- -rrb- yet when a most violent struggle and brilliant victory have take place the emperor nevertheless refuse the petition of the soldier for money make this statement : whatever excess they obtain above the customary amount will be wring from the blood of they parent and they kinsman for respect the fate of the empire heaven alone can decide -- and he rule they so temperately and firmly that even in the course of so many and great war he be impel neither by flattery nor by fear to do aught that be unfitting -lrb- sidenote : ad 172 -lrb- au 925 -rrb- -rrb- after conquer they marcus receive the title of germanicus we give the name german to those who dwell in the northern region -lrb- sidenote : -- 4 -- -rrb- the so-called bucolus begin a disturbance in egypt and under the leadership of isidorus a priest -lrb- footnote : omit -lrb- greek : kaus -rrb- -rrb- cause the rest of the egyptian to revolt they have first array in woman 's garment deceive the roman centurion make he think that they be bucoli woman and want to give he gold piece in exchange for they husband and then striking he down when he approach they he companion they sacrifice and after take a common oath over he entrails they devour they isidorus surpass in bribery all he contemporary next have conquer the roman in egypt in regular battle they come very near capture alexandrium and would have do so have not cassius be send against they from syrium as direct general he succeed in spoil the concord that exist among they and sunder they one from another for on account of they number and desperation he have not venture to attack they unite so when they fall into factional dispute he easily subdue they -lrb- sidenote : -- 5 -- -rrb- now it be in marcus 's war against the german -lrb- if mention ought to be make of these matter -rrb- that a captive lad on be ask some question by he rejoin : i can not answer you because of the cold so if you want to find out anything command that a coat be give I if you have one -- and a soldier one night who be do guard duty on the ister hear a shout of he fellow-soldier in captivity on the other side at once swim the stream just as he be release they and bring they back one prefect of marcus 's be bassaeus rufus a good man on the whole but uneducated and boorish have be bring up in poverty in he early youth -lrb- wherefore he have be disincline to go on the campaign and what marcus say be incomprehensible to he -rrb- once some one have interrupted he in the midst of trim a vine that wind about a tree and when he do not come down at the first bidding the person rebuke he and say : come down there prefect this he say think to humiliate he for he previous haughtiness yet later fortune give he this title to wear -lrb- sidenote : -- 6 -- -rrb- the emperor as often as he have leisure from war hold court and use to order that a most liberal supply of water be measure out for the speaker -lrb- footnote : this refer to the contrivance know as the clepsydra or water-clock which measure time by the slow drop of water from a upper into a lower vessel somewhat on the plan of the hour-glass -rrb- he make inquiry and answer of greater length so that exact justice be ensure by every possible expedient when thus engage he would often hold court to try the same case for eleven or even twelve day and sometimes -lrb- sidenote : ad 172 -lrb- au 926 -rrb- -rrb- at night he be industrious and apply himself diligently to all the duty of he office and there be nothing which he say or write or do that he regard a minor matter but sometimes he would consume whole day on the finest point put into practice he belief that the emperor should do nothing hurriedly for he think that if he should slight even the smallest detail it would bring he reproach that would overshadow all he other achievement yet he be so frail in body that at first he could not endure the cold but when the soldier have already come together in obedience to order he would retire before speak a word to they and he take but very little food always and that at night it be never he custom to eat during the daytime unless it be some of the drug call theriac -lrb- footnote : see galen on antidote book two chapter 17 and on theriac -lrb- to piso -rrb- chapter 2 -rrb- this drug he take not so much because he fear anything as because he stomach and chest be in bad condition and it be related that this practice enable he to endure the disease as well as other hardship -lrb- sidenote : ad 172 -lrb- -rrb- 173 -lrb- -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 7 -- -rrb- the iazyge be conquer by the roman on land at this time and subsequently on the river by this i mean not that any naval battle take place but that the roman follow they as they flee over the frozen ister and fight there as on dry land the iazyge perceive that they be be pursue await the foe 's onset expect easily to overcome they since they opponent be not accustom to ice accordingly some of the barbarian dash straight at they while other ride around to attack the flank for they horse be train to run safely even over a surface of this kind the roman see this be not alarmed but make a close formation place themselves so as to face all of they at once the majority lay down they shield and rest one foot upon they so that they might slip less receive the enemy 's assault some seize bridle other shield and spear-shaft and draw they towards they then become involve in close conflict they knock down both man and horse for on account of they momentum the enemy could not help slip the roman also slip down : but in case one of they fall on he back he drag he adversary down on top of he and then by wind he leg about he as in a wrestling match would get he underneath and if one fall on he face he make he opponent fall before he do also on he face the barbarian be unused to a contest of this sort and have lighter equipment be unable to resist so that but few escape out of a large force -lrb- sidenote : ad 174 -lrb- au 927 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 8 -- -rrb- so marcus make the marcomanus and iazyge subservient by a series of great struggle and danger a great war against the so-called quadus also fall to he lot and it be he good fortune to win a unexpected victory or rather it be give he from heaven at a time when the roman have run into danger in the battle the heavenly power most unexpectedly save they the quadus have surround they at a opportune spot and the roman be fight valiantly with they shield lock together : and the barbarian cease fight expect to capture they enemy easily by heat and thirst so they post guard all about and hem they in to prevent they get water anywhere for the barbarian be far superior in number the roman fall into dire distress from they fatigue and wound and the sun 's heat and they thirst and for these reason could neither fight nor march in any direction but be stand and be scorch in line of battle and at they several post when suddenly number of cloud rush together and a great rain certainly of divine origin come pour down indeed there be a story that arnouphi a egyptian wizard who be a companion of marcus invoke by means of enchantment various deity and in particular mercury god of the air and by this mean attract the rain -lrb- sidenote : -- 9 -- -rrb- this be what dio say about it but he seem to be tell a untruth whether voluntarily or involuntarily i be more inclined to think it be voluntarily it surely must be so for he be not ignorant of the fact that one company of the soldier have the special name of the thunderbolt -lrb- he mention it in the list along with the rest -rrb- -lrb- footnote : the reference be evidently to book fifty-five chapter 23 but it should be observe that the name though very possibly have the same sense be not identical the legion be here call -lrb- greek : keraunobolo -rrb- -lrb- = fulminatrix or fulmina -rrb- but in 55 23 -lrb- greek : keraunophoro -rrb- -lrb- = fulminifera -rrb- -rrb- and this be due to no other cause -lrb- nor be any other report -rrb- save that event which give rise to the title in this very war -- a event which enable the roman to survive on this occasion and bring destruction upon the barbarian it be not arnouphi the wizard for marcus be not account to have take pleasure in the company of wizard and charm but what i have reference to be as follow : marcus have a company -lrb- and the roman name for company be legion -rrb- of soldier from melitene they be all worshiper of christ now it be state that in that battle when marcus be in a quandary over have be surround and fear the loss of he whole army the prefect approach he and say that those call christian can accomplish anything whatever by they prayer and that among they there chance to be a whole company of this sect marcus on hearing this make a appeal to they to pray to they god and when they have pray the god immediately give ear hurl a thunderbolt upon the enemy and encourage the roman with rain marcus be astounded at what happen and honor the christian by a official decree while the legion he name the thunderbolt it be say also that there be a letter of marcus extant on this matter but the greek though they know that the company be call thunderbolt and bear witness to the fact themselves make no statement whatever about the reason for the appellation -lrb- sidenote : -- 10 -- -rrb- dio go on to say that when the rain pour down at first all bent they face upward and receive it in they mouth then some hold they shield and they helmet as pail and they themselves take fullmouthed draught of it and give they horse to drink the barbarian make a charge upon they they drink and fight at the same time and some who be wound gulp down together the water and the blood that flow into they helmet the most of they have give so much attention to drinking that they would have suffer some great damage from the enemy 's onset have not a violent hail and number of thunderbolt fall upon the latter 's rank in the same spot one might see water and fire descend from heaven at the same time : the one side be be drench and drink the other be be burn with fire and die the fire do not touch the roman but if it fall anywhere among they it be straightway extinguish on the other hand the shower do the barbarian no good but like oil serve rather to feed the flame that feed on they and they search for water while in the midst of rain some wound themselves in the attempt to put out the fire with blood and other run over to the side of the roman convince that they alone have the saving water marcus finally take pity on they he be for the seventh time salute as imperator by the soldier and although he be not wont to accept any such honor before the senate vote it -lrb- footnote : cp mommsen _ staatsrecht _ 12 p 123 -lrb- or 13 p 124 -rrb- also iii p 1108 -rrb- nevertheless this time he take it under the assumption that it be bestow from heaven and he send a despatch to that effect to the senate -- moreover faustina be name mother of the legion -lrb- sidenote : -- 11 -- -rrb- -lrb- marcus -lrb- antoninus -rrb- remain in pannonium in order to transact business with the embassy of the barbarian many come to he also at this time some promise a alliance : they be lead by battarius a child twelve year old and they receive money and succeed in restrain tarbus a neighbor potentate who have come into dacium be demand money and threaten to make war if he should not get it other like the quadus be ask for peace and they obtain it the emperor 's purpose be to have they detach from the marcomanus another reason be that they give horse and cattle surrender all the deserter and the captive at first to the number of thirteen thousand though later they promise to restore the remainder as well however the right of free intercourse even at market be not grant they the intention be to prevent the iazyge and the marcomanus whom they have swear not to receive nor let pass through they country from either mingle with they or present themselves also in the guise of quadus -- a plan which would enable they to reconnoitre the roman position and to purchase provision besides these who come to marcus many other despatch envoy some by tribe and some by nation offer to surrender themselves some of they be send on campaign to other part of the world and the captive and deserter who be fit for it be similarly treat other receive land in dacium or in pannonium or in moesium and germany or in italy itself a few of they who settle at ravenna make a uprising and even dare to take possession of the city : and for this reason he do not again bring any barbarian into italy but make even those who have previously come there find home outside -rrb- detachment of both astingus and lacringus have come to lend assistance to marcus -lrb- sidenote : -- 12 -- -rrb- -lrb- the astingus whose leader be raus and raptus come into dacium to settle in the hope of receive both money and land in return for term of alliance as they do not obtain this they put they wife and child in the keep of clemen -lrb- footnote : _ sex cornelius clemen _ -rrb- with the apparent intention of acquire the land of the costoboccus by force of arm and upon conquer they they injure dacium no less the lacringus fear that clemen out of dread might lead these newcomer into the land which they be inhabit attack they off they guard and win a decisive victory as a result the astingus commit no further deed display hostility to the roman but by make urgent supplication to marcus receive money from he and ask that land might be give they if they should harm in some way he temporary enemy now these perform some of they promise the cotinus make similar proposition but upon get control of tarrutenius paternus secretary of the emperor 's latin letter under the pretext of require he aid for a campaign against the marcomanus they not only fail to take this course but do he frightful injury and thereby ensure they own destruction later -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 171 -lrb- au 924 -rrb- -rrb- when in one battle the marcomanus be successful and kill marcus vindex the prefect he erect three statue in he memory -lrb- sidenote : -- 13 -- -rrb- -lrb- envoy be also send to marcus by the iazyge request peace but they do not obtain any for marcus know they race to be untrustworthy and furthermore because he have be deceive by the quadus wish to annihilate they absolutely -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- greek : exelein -rrb- -lrb- boissevain -rrb- in place of the m -lrb- greek : exelthein -rrb- -rrb- the quadus have not only make alliance at this time with the iazyge but previously too be wont to receive in they own land marcomanian fugitive who might be hard press while that tribe be at war with the roman nor do they do aught else that they have agree for they do not restore all the captive but only a few and these be such as they could not sell nor use for any work as helper and whenever they do give back any of those in good condition they would keep they relative at home in order that the man give up might desert again to join they friend they also expel they king furtius and on they own responsibility make ariogaesus king instead consequently the emperor do not confirm he since he have not be legally install nor renew the treaty of peace though they promise to return fifty thousand captive if he would -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 14 -- -rrb- -lrb- against ariogaesus marcus be so bitter that he issue a proclamation to the effect that any one who would bring he alive should receive a thousand gold piece and any one who kill he and exhibit he head five hundred yet in other case this emperor be always accustom to treat even he most stubborn foe humanely for instance he do not kill but merely send to britain tiridate a satrap who rouse a tumult in armenia and the person who slew the king of the heniochus and then hold the sword in verus 's -lrb- footnote : _ p martius verus _ -rrb- face when the latter rebuke he for it this then show the extent of he irritation against ariogaesus at the time however when the man be later capture he do he no harm but send he away to alexandrium -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 174 -lrb- -rrb- 175 -lrb- -rrb- -rrb- when pertinax in consideration of he brave exploit obtain the consulship there be nevertheless some who show displeasure at the fact that he be of obscure family and quote the line from tragedy : such thing the wretched war bring in its train -lrb- footnote : from euripide the suppliant verse 119 -rrb- they do not know that he should yet be sovereign -lrb- sidenote : ad 176 -lrb- -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 15 -- -rrb- -lrb- at the request of the marcomanus as express by they envoy and in view of the fact that they have follow all the injunction lay upon they even if sullenly and hesitatingly he release to they one half of the adjoining territory so that they could settle for a distance of about thirty-eight stade -lrb- footnote : or five mile -rrb- from the ister and establish the place and the day for they meeting together -lrb- these have not be previously determine -rrb- and he exchange hostage with they -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 175 -lrb- au 928 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 16 -- -rrb- -lrb- the iazyge also when they have experience reverse come to a agreement zanticus himself appear as suppliant before antoninus previously they have imprison banadaspus they second king for make proposal to he now however all the foremost man come in company with zanticus and make the same compact as that accept by the quadus and the marcomanus except in so far as they be require -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- greek : aemellon -rrb- -lrb- boissevain -rrb- -rrb- to dwell twice as far away from the ister as those tribe it be he wish to root they out utterly that they be still strong at this time and could have do the roman great harm be evident from the fact that they give back one hundred thousand captive out of a body in which many have be sell many be dead and many have run away and be recapture they supply antoninus at once with a cavalry force of eight thousand ally fifty-five hundred of whom he send to britain -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 17 -- -rrb- -lrb- the revolt of cassius and syrium force marcus antoninus even contrary to he wish to come to term with the iazyge he be so upset at the news that he do not even communicate to the senate the basis of the reconciliation make with they as he be wont to do in all other case -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 179-180 -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 18 -- -rrb- -lrb- the iazyge send a embassy and ask to be release from some of the agreement they have make and a certain leniency be show they to prevent they be entirely alienate yet neither they nor the burus be willing to join the roman alliance until they receive pledge from marcus that he would without fail prosecute the war to the uttermost they be afraid that he might make a treaty with the quadus as before and leave enemy dwelling at they door -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 19 -- -rrb- -lrb- marcus give audience to such person as come in the capacity of envoy from outside nation but all be not receive on the same footing this vary accord as the individual state be worthy to receive citizenship or freedom from tax or perpetual or temporary exemption from tribute or to enjoy permanent support and when the iazyge prove themselves most useful to he he release they from many of the restriction impose upon they -- indeed from all save from the arrangement make in regard to they gathering and mutual intercourse and the provision that they should _ not _ use boat of they own and _ should _ keep away from the island in the ister and he permit they to go through dacium and have dealings with the rhoxolanus as often as the governor of dacium would give they permission -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 20 -- -rrb- -lrb- the quadus and the marcomanus send envoy to marcus say that the two myriad of soldier that be in the fort would not allow -lrb- footnote : supply with reiske -lrb- greek : epetrepon -rrb- -rrb- they to pasture or till the soil or do anything else with freedom but keep receive many deserter from they and captive of theirs yet the soldier themselves be endure no great hardship inasmuch as they have bath-house and all necessary provision in abundance the quadus consequently would not endure the watch keep on they from fortification and undertake to withdraw _ en masse _ to the territory of the semnone but antoninus learn beforehand of they intention and by bar the road thither prevent they this show that he desire not to acquire they territory but to punish the member of the tribe -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 21 -- -rrb- -lrb- and the naristus have encounter hardship desert to the number of three thousand at once and receive land in we territory -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 22 -- -rrb- upon the rebellion of cassius in syrium marcus in great alarm summon he son commodus from rome since he be now able to enter the rank of the iuvene now cassius who be a syrian from cyrrhus have show himself a excellent man and the sort of person one would desire to have as emperor : only he be a son of one heliodorus -lrb- footnote : _ c avidius heliodorus _ -lrb- cp book sixty-nine chapter 3 -rrb- -rrb- who have be delight to secure the governorship of egypt as a result of he oratorical skill but in this uprising he make a terrible mistake and it be all due to he have be deceive by faustina the latter who be a daughter of antoninus pius see that she husband have fall ill and expect that he might die at any moment be afraid that the imperial office might revert to some outsider and she be leave in private life for commodus be both young and rather callow besides so she secretly induce cassius to make preparation to the end that if anything should happen to antoninus he might take both she and the sovereignty -lrb- sidenote : -- 23 -- -rrb- now while he be in this frame of mind a message come that marcus be dead -lrb- in such circumstance report always make matter worse than they really be -rrb- and immediately without wait to confirm the rumor he lay claim to the empire on the ground that it have be bestow upon he by the soldier at this time quarter in pannonium and in spite of the fact that before long he learn the truth nevertheless since he have once make a move he would not change he attitude but speedily win over the whole district bound by the taurus and be make preparation to maintain he ascendancy by war marcus on be inform of he uprising by verus the governor of cappadocium for a time conceal it but as the soldier be be mightily disturb by the report and be do a deal of talk he call they together and read a address of the follow nature : -lrb- sidenote : -- 24 -- -rrb- fellow-soldier i have not come before you to express indignation nor yet in a spirit of lamentation why rage against fate that be all-powerful but perchance it be needful to bewail the lot of those who be undeservedly unfortunate a lot which be now mine be it not afflict for we to meet war after war be it not absurd to be involve in civil conflict be not both these condition surpass in affliction and in absurdity by the proof before we that there be naught to be trust among mankind since i have be plot against by my dearest friend and have be thrust into a conflict against my will though i have commit no crime nor even error what virtue what friendship shall henceforth be deem secure after this experience of mine have not faith have not hope perish if the danger be mine alone i should give the matter no heed -- i be not bear to be immortal -- but since there have be a public secession -lrb- or rather obsession -rrb- and war be fasten its clutch upon all of we alike i should desire be it possible to invite cassius here and argue the case with he in you presence or in the presence of the senate and i would gladly without a contest withdraw from my office in he favor if this seem to be for the public advantage for it be on behalf of the public that i continue to toil and undergo danger and have spend so much time yonder outside of italy during mature manhood and now in old age and weakness though i can not take food without pain nor get sleep free from anxiety -lrb- sidenote : -- 25 -- -rrb- but since cassius would never be willing to agree to this -lrb- for how could he trust I after have show himself so untrustworthy towards I -rrb- you at least fellow-soldier ought to be of good cheer cilician syrian jew and egyptian have never prove you superior nor shall so prove even if they assemble in number ten time you own whereas they be now by the same proportion inferior nor yet would cassius himself now appear worthy of any particular consideration however much he may seem to possess the quality of generalship however many success he may seem to have gain a eagle be not formidable at the head of a army of daw nor a lion command fawn and it be not cassius but you that bring to a end the arabian or the famous parthian war again even though he be renown as a result of he achievement against the parthian yet you have verus who have win more victory than he and have acquire more territory in a not less but more distinguished manner -- but probably he have already change he mind on hearing that i be alive for surely he have do this on no other assumption than that i be dead and if he resist still further yet when he learn that we be approach he will surely hesitate both out of fear of you and out of respect for I -lrb- sidenote : -- 26 -- -rrb- there be only one thing i fear fellow-soldier -lrb- you shall be tell the whole truth -rrb- and that be that he may either kill himself because ashamed to come into we presence or some one else upon learn that i shall come and be set out against he may do it then should i be deprive of a great prize both of war and of victory and of a magnitude such as no human be ever yet obtain what be this why to forgive a man that have do you a injury to remain a friend to one who have transgress friendship to continue faithful to one who have break faith perhaps this seem strange to you but you ought not to disbelieve it for all goodness have not yet perish from among mankind but there be still in we a remnant of the ancient virtue and if any one do disbelieve it that render the more ardent my desire that man may see accomplished what no one would believe could come to pass that would be one profit i could derive from present ill if i could settle the affair well and show to all mankind that there be a right way to handle even civil war -lrb- sidenote : -- 27 -- -rrb- this be what marcus both say to the soldier and write to the senate in no place abuse cassius save he constantly term he ungrateful nor indeed do cassius ever utter or write anything of a nature insulting to marcus marcus at the time he be prepare for the war against cassius would accept no barbarian alliance although he find a concourse of foreign nation offer they service for he say that the barbarian ought not to know about trouble arise between roman while marcus be make preparation for the civil war many victory over various barbarian be report at one and the same time with the death of cassius the latter while walk have encounter antonius a centurion who give he a sudden wound in the neck though the blow be not entirely effective and antonius bear away by the impetus of he horse leave the deed incomplete so that he victim nearly escape but meantime the decurion have finish what be leave to do they cut off he head and set out to meet the emperor marcus antoninus -lrb- be so much grieve at the destruction of cassius that he would not even endure to see the sever head but before the murderer draw near give order that it should be bury -rrb- thus be this pretender slay after a dream of sovereignty lasting three month and six day and he son be murder somewhere else and marcus upon reach the province that have join in cassius 's uprising treat they all very kindly and put no one either obscure or prominent to death -lrb- sidenote : -- 28 -- -rrb- -lrb- the same man would not slay nor imprison nor do he put under any guard any one of the senator associate with cassius he do not so much as bring they before he own court but merely send they before the senate nominally under some other complaint and appoint they a fixed day on which to have they case hear of the rest he bring to justice a very few who have not only cooperate with cassius to the extent of some overt action but be personally guilty of some crime a proof of this be that he do not murder nor deprive of he property flavius calvisius the governor of egypt but merely confine he on a island the record make about he case marcus cause to be burn in order that no reproach might attach to he from they furthermore he release all he relative -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 176 -lrb- au 929 -rrb- -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 29 -- -rrb- about this same time faustina die either of the gout from which she have suffer or from less natural cause and to avoid be convict of she compact with cassius -- moreover marcus destroy the document -lrb- find in the chest of puden -rrb- -lrb- footnote : reimar suggest that perhaps puden be secretary of the greek letter of cassius as manlius -lrb- book seventy-two chapter 7 -rrb- be of he latin letter -rrb- not even read they in order that he might not learn even a name of any of the conspirator who have write something against he and that he might not -lrb- therefore -rrb- be reluctantly force to hate any one another account be that verus who be send ahead into syrium of which he have secure the governorship find they among the effect of cassius and put they out of the way say that this course would most probably be agreeable to the emperor but even if he should be angry it would be better that he -lrb- verus -rrb- himself should perish than many other marcus be so averse to slaughter that he see to it that the gladiator in rome contend without danger like athlete for he never permit any of they to have any sharp iron but they fight with blunt weapon round off at the end -lrb- and so far be he from countenance any slaughter that though at the request of the populace he order to be bring in a lion train to eat man he would not look at the beast nor emancipate its teacher in spite of the long-continued and urgent demand of the people instead he command proclamation to be make that the man have do nothing to deserve freedom -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 30 -- -rrb- in he great grief over the death of faustina he write to the senate that no one of those who have cooperate with cassius be dead as if in this fact alone he could find some consolation for faustina 's loss may it never happen he continue that any one of you be slay during -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- greek : ep emou -rrb- -lrb- dindorf -rrb- -rrb- my lifetime either by my vote or by you own finally he say : if i do not obtain this request i shall hasten on to death so pure and excellent and godfearing do he show himself throughout he career -lrb- nothing could force he to do anything inconsistent with he character neither the wickedness of daring attempt nor the expectation of similar event to follow as the result of pardon to such a extent do he refrain from invent any imaginary conspiracy and concoct any tragedy that have not take place that he release even those who most openly rise against he and take arm against he and against he son whether they be general or head of tribe or king and he put none of they to death either by he own action or by that of the senate or by any other arrangement whatever wherefore i actually believe that if he have capture cassius himself alive he would certainly have save he from injury -rrb- for he confer benefit upon many who have be murderer -- so far as lay in they power -- of himself and he son -lrb- sidenote : -- 31 -- -rrb- a law be at this time pass that no one should be governor in the province from which he have originally come because the revolt of cassius have occur during he administration of syrium which include he native district it be vote by the senate that silver image of marcus and faustina should be set up in the temple of venus and roma and that a altar should be erect whereon all the maiden marry in the city and they bridegroom should offer sacrifice also that a golden image of faustina should be carry in a chair to the theater on each occasion that the emperor should be a spectator and that it should be place in the seat well forward where she herself be wont to take she place when alive and that the woman of chief influence should all sit round about it -lrb- sidenote : -- 32 -- -rrb- marcus go to athen where after be initiate into the mystery he bestow honor upon the athenian and give teacher to all man in athen for every species of knowledge these teacher to receive a annual salary on he return to rome he make a address to the people and while he be say among other thing that he have be absent many year they cry out : eight and indicate this also with they hand in order that they might receive a equal number of gold piece for a banquet he smile and himself utter the word eight after that he distribute to they two hundred denarius apiece more than they have ever receive before -- in addition to do this he forgive all person all they debt to the imperial and to the public treasury for a space of forty-six year outside of the sixteen grant by hadrian and all the document relate to these debt he order burn in the forum -lrb- sidenote : ad 177 -lrb- au 930 -rrb- -rrb- -- he give money to many city one of they be smyrna that have suffer terribly by a earthquake he also assign the duty of build up this place to a ex-praetor of senatorial rank therefore i be surprise at the censure even now pass upon he to the effect that he be not a man of large calibre for whereas in ordinary matter he be really quite frugal he never demur at a single necessary expenditure -lrb- though as i have say -lrb- footnote : the reference here make by dio may very possibly be to a passage reproduce by zonara -lrb- xii 1 -rrb- : yet he be not thereby induce to secure money from the subject nation on one occasion indeed with war impend he have come short for fund and still do not devise any new tax nor endure to ask money from any one instead he expose in the forum all the heirloom of the palace even down to this or that piece of finery belong to he wife and solicit they purchase by any person so disposed this bring he a store of coin which he distribute to the soldier by success in the war he gain many time the amount in question and he issue a proclamation to the effect than any one so disposed among the purchaser of the imperial property might return the article purchase and receive its value some do so but the majority decline and nobody be compel to restore any object thus acquire -rrb- he hurt no one by levy -rrb- and he necessarily lay out very large sum beyond the ordinary requirement -lrb- sidenote : -- 33 -- -rrb- the scythian imbroglio which need he attention cause he to give he son a wife crispina sooner than he actually wish the quintilius could not end the war although there be two of they and they possess prudence courage and considerable experience consequently the ruler themselves be force to take the field -lrb- sidenote : ad 178 -lrb- au 931 -rrb- -rrb- marcus also ask the senate for money from the public treasury not because it have not be place in the sovereign 's authority but because marcus be wont to declare that this and everything else belong to the senate and the people we say he -lrb- speak to the senate -rrb- be so far from have anything of we own that we even live in a house of yours he set out therefore after these remark and after hurl the bloody spear that lay in the temple of bellona into hostile territory -lrb- i hear this from man who accompany he -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : ad 179 -rrb- paternus be give a large detachment and send to the scene of fight the barbarian hold out the entire day but be all cut down by the roman and marcus be for the tenth time salute as imperator -lrb- sidenote : ad 180 -lrb- au 933 -rrb- -rrb- have he live longer he would have subdue the whole region : as it be he pass away on the seventeenth of march not from the effect of the sickness that he have at the time but by the connivance of he physician as i have hear on good evidence who want to do a favor to commodus -lrb- sidenote : -- 34 -- -rrb- when at the point of death he commend he son to the protection of the soldier -lrb- for he do not wish he death to appear to be he fault -rrb- and to the military tribune who ask he for the watchword he say : go to the rise sun : i be already set after he be dead he obtain many mark of honor and be set up in gold within the senate-house itself so this be the manner of marcus 's demise -lrb- who besides all other virtue be so godfearing that even on the die nefastus he sacrifice at home and he rule better than any that have ever be in power to be sure he could not display many feat of physical prowess yet in he own person he make a very strong body out of a very weak one -rrb- most of he life he pass in the service of beneficence and therefore he erect on the capitol a temple to that goddess and call she by a most peculiar name which have never before be current -lrb- footnote : what this name be no one know sylburgius conjecture that it might be _ aequanimita _ -rrb- he himself refrain from all offence -lrb- and commit no fault voluntarily : -rrb- but the offence of other particularly those of he wife he endure and neither investigate they nor punish they in case any person do anything good he would praise he and use he for the service in which he excel but about other he do not trouble himself -lrb- say : it be impossible for one to create such man as one wish to have but it be proper to employ those in existence for that in which each of they may be useful to the commonwealth -rrb- that all he action be prompt not by pretence but by real virtue be strikingly clear he live fifty-eight year ten month and twenty-two day and of this time he have spend considerable as assistant to the previous antoninus and have himself be emperor nineteen year and eleven day yet from first to last he remain the same and change not a particle so truly be he a good man without any pretence about he -lrb- sidenote : -- 35 -- -rrb- he be vastly help by he education be a expert in rhetoric and in philosophical argument in the one he have cornelius fronto and claudius herode for teacher and in the other junius rusticus and apollonius of nicomedea -lrb- footnote : since apollonius be really from chalcedon a error may here charge to dio 's or some one else 's account -rrb- both of whom follow zeno 's school as a result great number pretend to engage in philosophy in order that they might be enrich by the emperor after all however he owe he great attainment chiefly to he natural disposition for even before he enjoy the society of those man he be unflinchingly set upon virtue while still a boy he delight all he relation who be numerous and influential and wealthy and be love by all of they this most of all lead hadrian to adopt he into he family and marcus for he part do not grow haughty -lrb- but though young and a caesar he dutifully play the part of servant to antoninus through all the latter 's reign and ungrudgingly do honor to the other man of eminence before go to see he father he use to greet the most worthy man in the house near the tiber where he live and in the very apartment where he sleep and all this time instead of wear the attire allow by he rank he go dress as a private citizen he visit many who be sick and invariably meet he teacher at the proper time dark garment be what he wear on go out when not in he father 's company and he never use the attendant for himself alone upon be appoint leader of the knight he enter the forum with the rest although he be caesar this show how excellent be he own natural disposition though it be aid to the greatest degree by education -rrb- he be always steep in greek and latin rhetorical and philosophical learning -lrb- though he have reach man 's estate and have hope of become emperor -rrb- -lrb- sidenote : -- 36 -- -rrb- before he be make caesar he have a dream in which he seem to have shoulder and hand of ivory and to use they in all respects as he do he real limb as a result of he great labor and study he be extremely frail in body yet from the very start he enjoy such good health that he use to fight in armor and on a hunt strike down wild boar while on horseback -lrb- and not only in he early youth but even later he write most of he letter to he intimate friend with he own hand -rrb- however he do not meet the good fortune that he deserve for he be not strong -lrb- in body -rrb- and be involve in the greatest variety of trouble throughout practically the whole period that he be ruler but i be sure i admire he all the more for this very reason that amid unusual and extraordinary happening he both himself survive and preserve the empire one thing in particular contribute to he lack of happiness -- the fact that after rear and educate he son in the best possible way he be monstrously disappoint in he this matter must now form the subject of we discourse for we history now descend from a kingdom of gold to one of iron and rust -lrb- footnote : reading -lrb- relieve they of the requirement of a annual levy however he issue further order that they should not assemble often nor in many part of the country but once each month in one place in the presence of they have live together so they die together and one child as well they have exhibit the most striking example ever see of affection for each other and at no time have they be divide even in they political office they have grow prosperous and exceedingly wealthy and be wont to govern together and to assist each other in try case at law sextus condianus son of maximus who surpass the generality roman legion proceed to commit many outrage and cut down a general together with the soldier that he have commodus be seize with fear and send marcellus ulpius against they this man who be temperate and frugal and always follow strict military rule in regard to food and all other detail when he be at war become in course of time haughty and arrogant he be conspicuously incorruptible in the matter of bribe but be not of a pleasant or kindly nature he show himself more wakeful than any other general and as he desire he associate also to be alert he write order on twelve tablet -lrb- such as be fill and -rrb- in order to avoid satisfy he hunger even with bread he send to rome for the loaf : -lrb- this be not because he could not eat what be prepare in that region but -rrb- it be do with the anything do not go to suit they lay the blame upon perenni and cherish anger against he the soldier in britain choose priscus a lieutenant emperor but he deprecate they action say i be as little suit commodus meet after rule twelve year nine month and fourteen day he have live thirty-one year and four month and with he the imperial house of the true aurelius cease -lrb- sidenote : -- 23 -- -rrb- after this there occur most violent war and factional disturbance the compilation of fact in this work of mine have be due to the follow chance i have write and publish a book about the dream and sign which cause severus to expect the imperial power and he happen to look at a copy that be send he by I write I a long and complimentary acknowledgment this letter i receive about nightfall and soon after go to sleep and in my slumber heaven command I that a history be write so it come about that i write the narrative with which i be at this moment concerned and because it pleased severus himself and other people very much i then conceive a desire to compile a record of all other matter of roman interest therefore i decide no longer to leave that treatise as a separate composition but to incorporate it in this present history in order that in one undertaking i might write positively everything from the beginning as far as fortune see fit to permit i have obtain this goddess it appear as the guide of the conduct of my life and therefore i be dependent on she entirely : she give I strength for my historical research when i be respectful and subdue before she and win I back to work by means of dream when i be discourage and give up the task : she grant I delightful hope in regard to the future that time will allow this history to survive and never let its brightness be dim to gather a account of everything do by the roman from the beginning until the death of severus have take I ten year and to arrange it in literary form twelve year more the rest will be write as opportunity offer -lrb- sidenote : -- 24 -- -rrb- prior to the death of commodus there be the follow sign many ill-boding eagle wander about the capitol utter cry that portend naught of peace and a crooked route they be sure to command both side of any attack party of the entire circuit the part on the land side reach a great height so as to repel any who come that way : the portion next to the tower project far out on each side make approach impossible for the enemy and in fine the bosporus be of the greatest aid to the citizen it be quite inevitable that once any person become entangled in life two year after this he take with he very great sum of money -lrb- sidenote : -- 12 -- -rrb- there be two principal race of the briton -- the caledonian and the maeatian the title of the rest have all be reduce to these two the maeatian live near the cross wall which cut the island in two and the caledonian be behind they both inhabit wild and waterless mountain desolate and swampy plain hold no wall nor city nor tilled field but live by pasturage and hunting and a few fruit tree the fish which be inexhaustible and past computing for multitude they do not taste they dwell coatless and shoeless in tent possess they woman in common and rear all the offspring as a community they form of government be mostly democratic and they be very fond of plunder consequently they choose they boldest spirit as leader they go into battle on chariot with small swift horse there be also infantry very quick at run and very firm in stand they ground they weapon be shield and short spear with a bronze apple attach to the end of the ground-spike so that when the instrument be shake it may clash and inspire the enemy with terror they also have dagger they can endure hunger and cold and any kind of wretchedness they plunge into the swamp and exist there for many day with only they head above water and in the forest they support themselves upon bark and root and in all -lrb- footnote : have state -rrb- -lrb- footnote : compare book thirty-nine chapter 50 which in turn refer to book sixty-six chapter 20 -rrb- be clearly prove at this time the length of it be seven thousand one send for the jar a little before he death and after feel it over remark : thou shalt hold a man that the world could not hold -lrb- sidenote : -- 16 -- -rrb- he be slow-moulded but strong though he eventually grow very weak from gout : mentally he be very keen and very firm he wish for more education than he get and for this reason he be sagacious rather than a good talker toward friend not forgetful to enemy most oppressive he be capable of everything that he desire to accomplish but careless of everything say about he hence he gather money from every source -lrb- save that he kill no one to get it -rrb- -lrb- and meet all necessary expenditure quite ungrudgingly he restore very many of the ancient building and inscribe upon they he own name to signify that he have repair they so though he expense be enormous he leave behind not merely a few myriad denarius easily reckon but a great many again he rebuke such person as be not chaste even go to the extent of enact certain law in they case he too cease to trouble he head about it apropo of this a quite witty remark be report of the wife of argentocoxus a caledonian to julium augusta when the latter after the treaty be joke she about the free intercourse of she sex in britain with man thereupon the foreigner assert : we fulfill the necessity of nature in a much better way than you roman woman we have dealings openly with the best man whereas you let yourselve be debauch in secret by the vilest this be what the british woman say -lrb- sidenote : -- 17 -- -rrb- the follow be the style of life that severus lead in time of peace he be sure to be do something before dawn while it be still night and after this he would go to walk tell and hearing of the interest of the empire then he hold court and separately -lrb- unless there be some great festival -rrb- and indeed he do this very well those on trial be allow plenty of water -lrb- footnote : the water-clock again compare book seventy-one chapter 6 -rrb- and he grant we he coadjutor full liberty to speak -- he continue to preside till noonday after that he go ride as much as he could next he take some kind of exercise and a bath he then consume a not meager lunch either by himself or with he child next as a rule he enjoy a nap later he rise attend to he remain duty of administration and while walk about occupied himself with discussion of both greek and latin lore then toward evening he would bathe again and dine with he attendant very seldom do he have any outsider to dinner and only on day when it be quite unavoidable do he arrange expensive banquet -- he live sixty-five year nine month and twenty-five day for he be bear on the eleventh of April of this he have rule seventeen year eight month and three day in fine he show himself so active that even
